<div><div class="result-pane--collapse-all-button--6dQHt"><button type="button" class="ud-btn ud-btn-medium ud-btn-ghost ud-btn-text-sm"><span class="ud-btn-label">Collapse all questions</span></button></div><div class="result-pane--question-result-pane-wrapper--2bGiz"><div class="result-pane--question-result-pane--sIcOh result-pane--accordion-panel--TEJg7"><div class="result-pane--question-header-wrapper--3DCpC"><div class="result-pane--question-header--pTUOx"><span class="result-pane--question-header-collapsed-text--WVdEr"><span class="result-pane--pane-title--f-2kd ud-heading-md"><span data-purpose="question-result-header-status-icon" class="result-pane--answer-status-icon--ebl6C"><span class="result-pane--question-icon-background--AskFJ" data-purpose="question-result-header-status-icon-background" style="background: oklch(0.7905 0.0283 281.19);"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-medium" style="color: oklch(0.7905 0.0283 281.19);"><use xlink:href="#icon-close"></use></svg></span></span><span>Question 1</span><span data-purpose="question-result-header-status-label" style="color: oklch(0.6722 0.0355 279.77);">Skipped</span></span><button type="button" class="ud-btn ud-btn-large ud-btn-ghost ud-btn-text-md ud-btn-icon ud-btn-icon-large"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-medium ud-icon-color-neutral"><use xlink:href="#icon-collapse"></use></svg></button></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="result-pane--question-format--PBvdY ud-text-md rt-scaffolding" id="question-prompt"><p>An IT security consultancy is working on a solution to protect data stored in Amazon S3 from any malicious activity as well as check for any vulnerabilities on Amazon EC2 instances.</p>

<p>As a solutions architect, which of the following solutions would you suggest to help address the given requirement?</p></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--question-result-pane-expanded-content--Og5Vc"><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-skipped--1NDPn" data-purpose="answer"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.6722 0.0355 279.77);"><use xlink:href="#icon-radio-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Use Amazon GuardDuty to monitor any malicious activity on data stored in Amazon S3. Use security assessments provided by Amazon GuardDuty to check for vulnerabilities on Amazon EC2 instances</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-skipped--1NDPn" data-purpose="answer"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.6722 0.0355 279.77);"><use xlink:href="#icon-radio-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Use Amazon Inspector to monitor any malicious activity on data stored in Amazon S3. Use security assessments provided by Amazon GuardDuty to check for vulnerabilities on Amazon EC2 instances</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-correct--PLOEU" data-purpose="answer"><div><span data-purpose="answer-result-header-user-label" class="result-pane--answer-by-user-label--PSH86 ud-heading-xs" style="background: oklch(0.8101 0.0873 162.22); color: oklch(0.3072 0.0555 158.67);">Correct answer</span></div><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.2565 0.0265 278.04);"><use xlink:href="#icon-radio-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Use Amazon GuardDuty to monitor any malicious activity on data stored in Amazon S3. Use security assessments provided by Amazon Inspector to check for vulnerabilities on Amazon EC2 instances</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-skipped--1NDPn" data-purpose="answer"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.6722 0.0355 279.77);"><use xlink:href="#icon-radio-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Use Amazon Inspector to monitor any malicious activity on data stored in Amazon S3. Use security assessments provided by Amazon Inspector to check for vulnerabilities on Amazon EC2 instances</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--question-related-fields--c3m--"><div class="overall-explanation-pane--overall-explanation--G-hLQ ud-form-group"><label class="ud-heading-md ud-form-label ud-heading-sm" for="form-group--136">Overall explanation</label><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-text-md rt-scaffolding" id="overall-explanation"><p>Correct option:</p>

<p><strong>Use Amazon GuardDuty to monitor any malicious activity on data stored in Amazon S3. Use security assessments provided by Amazon Inspector to check for vulnerabilities on Amazon EC2 instances</strong></p>

<p>Amazon GuardDuty offers threat detection that enables you to continuously monitor and protect your AWS accounts, workloads, and data stored in Amazon S3. GuardDuty analyzes continuous streams of meta-data generated from your account and network activity found in AWS CloudTrail Events, Amazon VPC Flow Logs, and DNS Logs. It also uses integrated threat intelligence such as known malicious IP addresses, anomaly detection, and machine learning to identify threats more accurately.</p>

<p>How Amazon GuardDuty works:
<img src="https://d1.awsstatic.com/product-marketing/Amazon%20GuardDuty/product-page-diagram-Amazon-GuardDuty_how-it-works.a4daf7e3aaf3532623a3797dd3af606a85fc2e7b.png" style="display: none;"><span class="ud-component--base-components--open-full-size-image"><div class="open-full-size-image--wrapper--R4gIm" data-purpose="open-full-size-image"><img src="https://d1.awsstatic.com/product-marketing/Amazon%20GuardDuty/product-page-diagram-Amazon-GuardDuty_how-it-works.a4daf7e3aaf3532623a3797dd3af606a85fc2e7b.png" alt="" loading="eager"><button type="button" class="ud-btn ud-btn-medium ud-btn-link ud-btn-text-sm open-full-size-image--backdrop--Zor3j"><svg aria-label="Larger image" role="img" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-large ud-icon-color-neutral"><use xlink:href="#icon-search"></use></svg></button></div></span>
via - <a href="https://aws.amazon.com/guardduty/">https://aws.amazon.com/guardduty/</a></p>

<p>Amazon Inspector security assessments help you check for unintended network accessibility of your Amazon EC2 instances and for vulnerabilities on those EC2 instances. Amazon Inspector assessments are offered to you as pre-defined rules packages mapped to common security best practices and vulnerability definitions.</p>

<p>Incorrect options:</p>

<p><strong>Use Amazon GuardDuty to monitor any malicious activity on data stored in Amazon S3. Use security assessments provided by Amazon GuardDuty to check for vulnerabilities on Amazon EC2 instances</strong></p>

<p><strong>Use Amazon Inspector to monitor any malicious activity on data stored in Amazon S3. Use security assessments provided by Amazon Inspector to check for vulnerabilities on Amazon EC2 instances</strong></p>

<p><strong>Use Amazon Inspector to monitor any malicious activity on data stored in Amazon S3. Use security assessments provided by Amazon GuardDuty to check for vulnerabilities on Amazon EC2 instances</strong></p>

<p>These three options contradict the explanation provided above, so these options are incorrect.</p>

The assets are accessed by a large number of users for the first few days and the frequency of access falls down drastically after a week. Although the assets would be accessed occasionally after the first week, but they must continue to be immediately accessible when required. The cost of maintaining all the assets on Amazon S3 storage is turning out to be very expensive and the agency is looking at reducing costs as much as possible.</p>

<p>As an AWS Certified Solutions Architect – Associate, can you suggest a way to lower the storage costs while fulfilling the business requirements?</p></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--question-result-pane-expanded-content--Og5Vc"><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-skipped--1NDPn" data-purpose="answer"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg Zone-Infrequent Access (S3 One Zone-IA) after 7 days</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-skipped--1NDPn" to transition the objects to Amazon S3 Standard-Infrequent Access (S3 Standard-IA) after 7 days</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div oklch(0.6722 0.0355 279.77);"><use xlink:href="#icon-radio-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-correct--PLOEU" data-purpose="answer"><div><span data-purpose="answer-result-header-user-label" class="result-pane--answer-by-user-label--PSH86 ud-heading-xs" style="background: oklch(0.8101 0.0873 162.22); color: oklch(0.3072 0.0555 158.67);">Correct answer</span></div><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.2565 0.0265 278.04);"><use xlink:href="#icon-radio-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Configure a lifecycle policy to transition the objects to Amazon S3 One Zone-Infrequent Access (S3 One Zone-IA) after 30 days</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--question-related-fields--c3m--"><div class="overall-explanation-pane--overall-explanation--G-hLQ ud-form-group"><label class="ud-heading-md ud-form-label ud-heading-sm" for="form-group--138">Overall explanation</label><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-text-md rt-scaffolding" id="overall-explanation"><p>Correct option:</p>

<p><strong>Configure a lifecycle policy to transition the objects to Amazon S3 One Zone-Infrequent Access (S3 One Zone-IA) after 30 days</strong></p>

<p>Amazon S3 One Zone-IA is for data that is accessed less frequently, but requires rapid access when needed. Unlike other S3 Storage Classes which store data in a minimum of three Availability Zones (AZs), Amazon S3 One Zone-IA stores data in a single Availability Zone (AZ) and costs 20% less than Amazon S3 Standard-IA. Amazon S3 One Zone-IA is ideal for customers who want a lower-cost option for infrequently accessed and re-creatable data but do not require the availability and resilience of Amazon S3 Standard or Amazon S3 Standard-IA. The minimum storage duration is 30 days before you can transition objects from Amazon S3 Standard to Amazon S3 One Zone-IA.</p>

<p>Amazon S3 One Zone-IA offers the same high durability, high throughput, and low latency of Amazon S3 Standard, with a low per GB storage price and per GB retrieval fee. S3 Storage Classes can be configured at the object level, and a single bucket can contain objects stored across Amazon S3 Standard, Amazon S3 Intelligent-Tiering, Amazon S3 Standard-IA, and Amazon S3 One Zone-IA. You can also use S3 Lifecycle policies to automatically transition objects between storage classes without any application changes.</p>

<p>Constraints for Lifecycle storage class transitions:
<img src="https://assets-pt.media.datacumulus.com/aws-saa-pt/assets/pt1-q8-i1.jpg" style="display: none;"><span class="ud-component--base-components--open-full-size-image"><div class="open-full-size-image--wrapper--R4gIm" data-purpose="open-full-size-image"><img src="https://assets-pt.media.datacumulus.com/aws-saa-pt/assets/pt1-q8-i1.jpg" alt="" loading="eager"><button type="button" class="ud-btn ud-btn-medium ud-btn-link ud-btn-text-sm open-full-size-image--backdrop--Zor3j"><svg aria-label="Larger image" role="img" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-large ud-icon-color-neutral"><use xlink:href="#icon-search"></use></svg></button></div></span>
via - <a href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AmazonS3/latest/dev/lifecycle-transition-general-considerations.html">https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AmazonS3/latest/dev/lifecycle-transition-general-considerations.html</a></p>

<p>Supported Amazon S3 lifecycle transitions:
<img src="https://assets-pt.media.datacumulus.com/aws-saa-pt/assets/pt1-q8-i2.jpg" style="display: none;"><span class="ud-component--base-components--open-full-size-image"><div class="open-full-size-image--wrapper--R4gIm" data-purpose="open-full-size-image"><img src="https://assets-pt.media.datacumulus.com/aws-saa-pt/assets/pt1-q8-i2.jpg" alt="" loading="eager"><button type="button" class="ud-btn ud-btn-medium ud-btn-link ud-btn-text-sm open-full-size-image--backdrop--Zor3j"><svg aria-label="Larger image" role="img" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-large ud-icon-color-neutral"><use xlink:href="#icon-search"></use></svg></button></div></span>
via - <a href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AmazonS3/latest/dev/lifecycle-transition-general-considerations.html">https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AmazonS3/latest/dev/lifecycle-transition-general-considerations.html</a></p>

<p>Incorrect options:</p>

<p><strong>Configure a lifecycle policy to transition the objects to Amazon S3 Standard-Infrequent Access (S3 Standard-IA) after 7 days</strong></p>

<p><strong>Configure a lifecycle policy to transition the objects to Amazon S3 One Zone-Infrequent Access (S3 One Zone-IA) after 7 days</strong></p>

<p>As mentioned earlier, the minimum storage duration is 30 days before you can transition objects from Amazon S3 Standard to Amazon S3 One Zone-IA or Amazon S3 Standard-IA, so both these options are added as distractors.</p>

<p><strong>Configure a lifecycle policy to transition the objects to Amazon S3 Standard-Infrequent Access (S3 Standard-IA) after 30 days</strong> - Amazon S3 Standard-IA is for data that is accessed less frequently, but requires rapid access when needed. S3 Standard-IA offers the high durability, high throughput, and low latency of Amazon S3 Standard, with a low per GB storage price and per GB retrieval fee. This combination of low cost and high performance makes Amazon S3 Standard-IA ideal for long-term storage, backups, and as a data store for disaster recovery files. But, it costs more than Amazon S3 One Zone-IA because of the redundant storage across Availability Zones (AZs). As the data is re-creatable, so you don't need to incur this additional cost.</p>

As this is sensitive health information, the backup of the user data must be kept encrypted in Amazon Simple Storage Service (Amazon S3). class="ud-heading-md ud-form-label ud-heading-sm" for="form-group--140">Overall explanation</label><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-text-md rt-scaffolding" id="overall-explanation"><p>Correct option:</p>

<p><strong>Use server-side encryption with AWS Key Management Service keys (SSE-KMS) to encrypt the user data on Amazon S3</strong></p>

<p>AWS Key Management Service (AWS KMS) is a service that combines secure, highly available hardware and software to provide a key management system scaled for the cloud. When you use server-side encryption with AWS KMS (SSE-KMS), you can specify a customer-managed CMK that you have already created.
SSE-KMS provides you with an audit trail that shows when your CMK was used and by whom. Therefore SSE-KMS is the correct solution for this use-case.</p>

<p>Server Side Encryption in S3:
<img src="https://assets-pt.media.datacumulus.com/aws-saa-pt/assets/pt1-q22-i1.jpg" style="display: none;"><span class="ud-component--base-components--open-full-size-image"><div class="open-full-size-image--wrapper--R4gIm" data-purpose="open-full-size-image"><img src="https://assets-pt.media.datacumulus.com/aws-saa-pt/assets/pt1-q22-i1.jpg" alt="" loading="eager"><button type="button" class="ud-btn ud-btn-medium ud-btn-link ud-btn-text-sm open-full-size-image--backdrop--Zor3j"><svg aria-label="Larger image" role="img" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-large ud-icon-color-neutral"><use xlink:href="#icon-search"></use></svg></button></div></span>
via - <a href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AmazonS3/latest/dev/serv-side-encryption.html">https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AmazonS3/latest/dev/serv-side-encryption.html</a></p>

<p>Incorrect options:</p>

<p><strong>Use server-side encryption with Amazon S3 managed keys (SSE-S3) to encrypt the user data on Amazon S3</strong> - When you use Server-Side Encryption with Amazon S3-Managed Keys (SSE-S3), each object is encrypted with a unique key. However this option does not provide the ability to audit trail the usage of the encryption keys.</p>

<p><strong>Use server-side encryption with customer-provided keys (SSE-C) to encrypt the user data on Amazon S3</strong> - With Server-Side Encryption with Customer-Provided Keys (SSE-C), you manage the encryption keys and Amazon S3 manages the encryption, as it writes to disks, and decryption when you access your objects. However this option does not provide the ability to audit trail the usage of the encryption keys.</p>

<p><strong>Use client-side encryption with client provided keys and then upload the encrypted user data to Amazon S3</strong> - Using client-side encryption is ruled out as the startup does not want to provide the encryption keys.</p>

The company's leaderboard requires high availability, low latency, and real-time processing to deliver customizable user data for the community of users working out together virtually from the comfort of their home.</p>

<p>As a solutions architect, which of the following solutions would you recommend? (Select two)</p></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--question-result-pane-expanded-content--Og5Vc"><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-skipped--1NDPn" data-purpose="answer"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.6722 0.0355 279.77);"><use xlink:href="#icon-checkbox-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Power the on-demand, live leaderboard using Amazon DynamoDB as it meets the in-memory, high availability, low latency requirements</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-correct--PLOEU" data-purpose="answer"><div><span data-purpose="answer-result-header-user-label" class="result-pane--answer-by-user-label--PSH86 ud-heading-xs" style="background: oklch(0.8101 0.0873 162.22); color: oklch(0.3072 0.0555 158.67);">Correct selection</span></div><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.2565 0.0265 278.04);"><use xlink:href="#icon-checkbox-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Power the on-demand, live leaderboard using Amazon ElastiCache for Redis as it meets the in-memory, high availability, low latency requirements</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-skipped--1NDPn" data-purpose="answer"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.6722 0.0355 279.77);"><use xlink:href="#icon-checkbox-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Power the on-demand, live leaderboard using Amazon RDS for Aurora as it meets the in-memory, high availability, low latency requirements</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-correct--PLOEU" data-purpose="answer"><div><span data-purpose="answer-result-header-user-label" class="result-pane--answer-by-user-label--PSH86 ud-heading-xs" style="background: oklch(0.8101 0.0873 162.22); color: oklch(0.3072 0.0555 158.67);">Correct selection</span></div><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.2565 0.0265 278.04);"><use xlink:href="#icon-checkbox-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Power the on-demand, live leaderboard using Amazon DynamoDB with DynamoDB Accelerator (DAX) as it meets the in-memory, high availability, low latency requirements</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-skipped--1NDPn" data-purpose="answer"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.6722 0.0355 279.77);"><use xlink:href="#icon-checkbox-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Power the on-demand, live leaderboard using Amazon Neptune as it meets the in-memory, high availability, low latency requirements</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--question-related-fields--c3m--"><div class="overall-explanation-pane--overall-explanation--G-hLQ ud-form-group"><label class="ud-heading-md ud-form-label ud-heading-sm" for="form-group--142">Overall explanation</label><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-text-md rt-scaffolding" id="overall-explanation"><p>Correct options:</p>

<p><strong>Power the on-demand, live leaderboard using Amazon ElastiCache for Redis as it meets the in-memory, high availability, low latency requirements</strong></p>

<p>Amazon ElastiCache for Redis is a blazing fast in-memory data store that provides sub-millisecond latency to power internet-scale real-time applications. Amazon ElastiCache for Redis is a great choice for real-time transactional and analytical processing use cases such as caching, chat/messaging, gaming leaderboards, geospatial, machine learning, media streaming, queues, real-time analytics, and session store.
ElastiCache for Redis can be used to power the live leaderboard, so this option is correct.</p>

<p>Amazon ElastiCache for Redis Overview:
<img src="https://d1.awsstatic.com/elasticache/EC_Use_Cases/product-page-diagram_ElastiCache_redis_how-it-works.eac60b60768c2a2041cc0b2673e7f5d2a0fef6a1.png" style="display: none;"><span class="ud-component--base-components--open-full-size-image"><div class="open-full-size-image--wrapper--R4gIm" data-purpose="open-full-size-image"><img src="https://d1.awsstatic.com/elasticache/EC_Use_Cases/product-page-diagram_ElastiCache_redis_how-it-works.eac60b60768c2a2041cc0b2673e7f5d2a0fef6a1.png" alt="" loading="eager"><button type="button" class="ud-btn ud-btn-medium ud-btn-link ud-btn-text-sm open-full-size-image--backdrop--Zor3j"><svg aria-label="Larger image" role="img" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-large ud-icon-color-neutral"><use xlink:href="#icon-search"></use></svg></button></div></span></p>

<p><strong>Power the on-demand, live leaderboard using Amazon DynamoDB with DynamoDB Accelerator (DAX) as it meets the in-memory, high availability, low latency requirements</strong></p>

<p>Amazon DynamoDB is a key-value and document database that delivers single-digit millisecond performance at any scale. It's a fully managed, multiregion, multimaster, durable database with built-in security, backup and restore, and in-memory caching for internet-scale applications.
DAX is a DynamoDB-compatible caching service that enables you to benefit from fast in-memory performance for demanding applications. So DynamoDB with DAX can be used to power the live leaderboard.</p>

<p>Incorrect options:</p>

<p><strong>Power the on-demand, live leaderboard using Amazon Neptune as it meets the in-memory, high availability, low latency requirements</strong> - Amazon Neptune is a fast, reliable, fully-managed graph database service that makes it easy to build and run applications that work with highly connected datasets. Neptune is not an in-memory database, so this option is not correct.</p>

<p><strong>Power the on-demand, live leaderboard using Amazon DynamoDB as it meets the in-memory, high availability, low latency requirements</strong> - DynamoDB is not an in-memory database, so this option is not correct.</p>

<p><strong>Power the on-demand, live leaderboard using Amazon RDS for Aurora as it meets the in-memory, high availability, low latency requirements</strong> - Amazon Aurora is a MySQL and PostgreSQL-compatible relational database built for the cloud, that combines the performance and availability of traditional enterprise databases with the simplicity and cost-effectiveness of open source databases. Amazon Aurora features a distributed, fault-tolerant, self-healing storage system that auto-scales up to 128TB per database instance. Aurora is not an in-memory database, so this option is not correct.</p>

The REST API stores the user data in Amazon DynamoDB and any static content, such as images, are served via Amazon Simple Storage Service (Amazon S3). On analyzing the usage trends, it is found that 90% of the read requests are for commonly accessed data across all users.</p>

<p>As a Solutions Architect, which of the following would you suggest as the MOST efficient solution to improve the application performance?</p></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--question-result-pane-expanded-content--Og5Vc"><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-correct--PLOEU" data-purpose="answer"><div><span data-purpose="answer-result-header-user-label" class="result-pane--answer-by-user-label--PSH86 ud-heading-xs" style="background: oklch(0.8101 0.0873 162.22); color: oklch(0.3072 0.0555 158.67);">Correct answer</span></div><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.2565 0.0265 278.04);"><use xlink:href="#icon-radio-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Enable Amazon DynamoDB Accelerator (DAX) for Amazon DynamoDB and Amazon CloudFront for Amazon S3</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-skipped--1NDPn" data-purpose="answer"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.6722 0.0355 279.77);"><use xlink:href="#icon-radio-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Enable ElastiCache Redis for DynamoDB and Amazon CloudFront for Amazon S3</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-skipped--1NDPn" data-purpose="answer"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.6722 0.0355 279.77);"><use xlink:href="#icon-radio-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Enable Amazon DynamoDB Accelerator (DAX) for Amazon DynamoDB and ElastiCache Memcached for Amazon S3</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-skipped--1NDPn" data-purpose="answer"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.6722 0.0355 279.77);"><use xlink:href="#icon-radio-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Enable ElastiCache Redis for DynamoDB and ElastiCache Memcached for Amazon S3</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--question-related-fields--c3m--"><div class="overall-explanation-pane--overall-explanation--G-hLQ ud-form-group"><label class="ud-heading-md ud-form-label ud-heading-sm" for="form-group--144">Overall explanation</label><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-text-md rt-scaffolding" id="overall-explanation"><p>Correct option:</p>

<p><strong>Enable Amazon DynamoDB Accelerator (DAX) for Amazon DynamoDB and Amazon CloudFront for Amazon S3</strong></p>

<p>Amazon DynamoDB Accelerator (DAX) is a fully managed, highly available, in-memory cache for Amazon DynamoDB that delivers up to a 10 times performance improvement—from milliseconds to microseconds—even at millions of requests per second.</p>

<p>Amazon DynamoDB Accelerator (DAX) is tightly integrated with Amazon DynamoDB—you simply provision a DAX cluster, use the DAX client SDK to point your existing Amazon DynamoDB API calls at the DAX cluster, and let DAX handle the rest. Because DAX is API-compatible with Amazon DynamoDB, you don't have to make any functional application code changes. DAX is used to natively cache Amazon DynamoDB reads.</p>

<p>Amazon CloudFront is a content delivery network (CDN) service that delivers static and dynamic web content, video streams, and APIs around the world, securely and at scale. By design, delivering data out of Amazon CloudFront can be more cost-effective than delivering it from S3 directly to your users.</p>

<p>When a user requests content that you serve with CloudFront, their request is routed to a nearby Edge Location. If CloudFront has a cached copy of the requested file, CloudFront delivers it to the user, providing a fast (low-latency) response. If the file they’ve requested isn’t yet cached, CloudFront retrieves it from your origin – for example, the Amazon S3 bucket where you’ve stored your content.</p>

<p>So, you can use Amazon CloudFront to improve application performance to serve static content from Amazon S3.</p>

<p>Incorrect options:</p>

<p><strong>Enable ElastiCache Redis for DynamoDB and Amazon CloudFront for Amazon S3</strong></p>

<p>Amazon ElastiCache for Redis is a blazing fast in-memory data store that provides sub-millisecond latency to power internet-scale real-time applications. Amazon ElastiCache for Redis is a great choice for real-time transactional and analytical processing use cases such as caching, chat/messaging, gaming leaderboards, geospatial, machine learning, media streaming, queues, real-time analytics, and session store.</p>

<p>Amazon ElastiCache for Redis Overview:
<img src="https://d1.awsstatic.com/elasticache/EC_Use_Cases/product-page-diagram_ElastiCache_redis_how-it-works.eac60b60768c2a2041cc0b2673e7f5d2a0fef6a1.png" style="display: none;"><span class="ud-component--base-components--open-full-size-image"><div class="open-full-size-image--wrapper--R4gIm" data-purpose="open-full-size-image"><img src="https://d1.awsstatic.com/elasticache/EC_Use_Cases/product-page-diagram_ElastiCache_redis_how-it-works.eac60b60768c2a2041cc0b2673e7f5d2a0fef6a1.png" alt="" loading="eager"><button type="button" class="ud-btn ud-btn-medium ud-btn-link ud-btn-text-sm open-full-size-image--backdrop--Zor3j"><svg aria-label="Larger image" role="img" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-large ud-icon-color-neutral"><use xlink:href="#icon-search"></use></svg></button></div></span>
via - <a href="https://aws.amazon.com/elasticache/redis/">https://aws.amazon.com/elasticache/redis/</a></p>

<p>Although you can integrate Redis with DynamoDB, it's much more involved than using DAX which is a much better fit.</p>

<p><strong>Enable Amazon DynamoDB Accelerator (DAX) for Amazon DynamoDB and ElastiCache Memcached for Amazon S3</strong></p>

<p><strong>Enable ElastiCache Redis for DynamoDB and ElastiCache Memcached for Amazon S3</strong></p>

<p>Amazon ElastiCache for Memcached is a Memcached-compatible in-memory key-value store service that can be used as a cache or a data store. Amazon ElastiCache for Memcached is a great choice for implementing an in-memory cache to decrease access latency, increase throughput, and ease the load off your relational or NoSQL database.</p>

<p>Amazon ElastiCache Memcached cannot be used as a cache to serve static content from Amazon S3, so both these options are incorrect.</p>

</div></div><div data-purpose="domain-pane" class="domain-pane--domain-pane--Pw9dK"><div class="domain-pane--domain-pane-header--2263m ud-heading-md">Domain</div><div class="ud-text-md">Design Cost-Optimized Architectures</div></div></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--question-result-pane-wrapper--2bGiz"><div class="result-pane--question-result-pane--sIcOh result-pane--accordion-panel--TEJg7"><div class="result-pane--question-header-wrapper--3DCpC"><div class="result-pane--question-header--pTUOx"><span class="result-pane--question-header-collapsed-text--WVdEr"><span class="result-pane--pane-title--f-2kd ud-heading-md"><span data-purpose="question-result-header-status-icon" class="result-pane--answer-status-icon--ebl6C"><span class="result-pane--question-icon-background--AskFJ" data-purpose="question-result-header-status-icon-background" style="background: oklch(0.7905 0.0283 281.19);"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-medium" style="color: oklch(0.7905 0.0283 281.19);"><use xlink:href="#icon-close"></use></svg></span></span><span>Question 6</span><span data-purpose="question-result-header-status-label" style="color: oklch(0.6722 0.0355 279.77);">Skipped</span></span><button type="button" class="ud-btn ud-btn-large ud-btn-ghost ud-btn-text-md ud-btn-icon ud-btn-icon-large"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-medium ud-icon-color-neutral"><use xlink:href="#icon-collapse"></use></svg></button></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="result-pane--question-format--PBvdY ud-text-md rt-scaffolding" id="question-prompt"><p>A technology blogger wants to write a review on the comparative pricing for various storage types available on AWS Cloud. The blogger has created a test file of size 1 gigabytes with some random data. Next he copies this test file into AWS S3 Standard storage class, provisions an Amazon EBS volume (General Purpose SSD (gp2)) with 100 gigabytes of provisioned storage and copies the test file into the Amazon EBS volume, and lastly copies the test file into an Amazon EFS Standard Storage filesystem. At the end of the month, he analyses the bill for costs incurred on the respective storage types for the test file.</p>

<p>What is the correct order of the storage charges incurred for the test file on these three storage types?</p></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--question-result-pane-expanded-content--Og5Vc"><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-correct--PLOEU" data-purpose="answer"><div><span data-purpose="answer-result-header-user-label" class="result-pane--answer-by-user-label--PSH86 ud-heading-xs" style="background: oklch(0.8101 0.0873 162.22); color: oklch(0.3072 0.0555 158.67);">Correct answer</span></div><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.2565 0.0265 278.04);"><use xlink:href="#icon-radio-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Cost of test file storage on Amazon S3 Standard &lt; Cost of test file storage on Amazon EFS &lt; Cost of test file storage on Amazon EBS</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-skipped--1NDPn" data-purpose="answer"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.6722 0.0355 279.77);"><use xlink:href="#icon-radio-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Cost of test file storage on Amazon EFS &lt; Cost of test file storage on Amazon S3 Standard &lt; Cost of test file storage on Amazon EBS</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-skipped--1NDPn" data-purpose="answer"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.6722 0.0355 279.77);"><use xlink:href="#icon-radio-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Cost of test file storage on Amazon S3 Standard &lt; Cost of test file storage on Amazon EBS &lt; Cost of test file storage on Amazon EFS</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-skipped--1NDPn" data-purpose="answer"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.6722 0.0355 279.77);"><use xlink:href="#icon-radio-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Cost of test file storage on Amazon EBS &lt; Cost of test file storage on Amazon S3 Standard &lt; Cost of test file storage on Amazon EFS</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--question-related-fields--c3m--"><div class="overall-explanation-pane--overall-explanation--G-hLQ ud-form-group"><label class="ud-heading-md ud-form-label ud-heading-sm" for="form-group--146">Overall explanation</label><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-text-md rt-scaffolding" id="overall-explanation"><p>Correct option:</p>

<p><strong>Cost of test file storage on Amazon S3 Standard &lt; Cost of test file storage on Amazon EFS &lt; Cost of test file storage on Amazon EBS</strong></p>

<p>With Amazon EFS, you pay only for the resources that you use. The Amazon EFS Standard Storage pricing is $0.30 per GB per month. Therefore the cost for storing the test file on EFS is $0.30 for the month.</p>

<p>For Amazon EBS General Purpose SSD (gp2) volumes, the charges are $0.10 per GB-month of provisioned storage. Therefore, for a provisioned storage of 100GB for this use-case, the monthly cost on EBS is $0.10*100 = $10. This cost is irrespective of how much storage is actually consumed by the test file.</p>

<p>For S3 Standard storage, the pricing is $0.023 per GB per month. Therefore, the monthly storage cost on S3 for the test file is $0.023.</p>

<p>Therefore this is the correct option.</p>

<p>Incorrect options:</p>

<p><strong>Cost of test file storage on Amazon S3 Standard &lt; Cost of test file storage on Amazon EBS &lt; Cost of test file storage on Amazon EFS</strong></p>

<p><strong>Cost of test file storage on Amazon EFS &lt; Cost of test file storage on Amazon S3 Standard &lt; Cost of test file storage on Amazon EBS</strong></p>

<p><strong>Cost of test file storage on Amazon EBS &lt; Cost of test file storage on Amazon S3 Standard &lt; Cost of test file storage on Amazon EFS</strong></p>

<p>Following the computations shown earlier in the explanation, these three options are incorrect.</p>

The company has defined different retention periods for different objects present in the Amazon S3 buckets, based on the compliance requirements. But, the retention rules do not seem to work as expected.</p>

<p>Which of the following options represent a valid configuration for setting up retention periods for objects in Amazon S3 buckets? (Select two)</p></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--question-result-pane-expanded-content--Og5Vc"><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-correct--PLOEU" data-purpose="answer"><div><span data-purpose="answer-result-header-user-label" class="result-pane--answer-by-user-label--PSH86 ud-heading-xs" id="answer-text"><p>The bucket default settings will override any explicit retention mode or period you request on an object version</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-skipped--1NDPn" data-purpose="answer"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>You cannot place a retention period on an object version through a bucket default setting</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-correct--PLOEU" data-purpose="answer"><div><span data-purpose="answer-result-header-user-label" class="result-pane--answer-by-user-label--PSH86 ud-heading-xs" style="background: oklch(0.8101 0.0873 162.22); color: oklch(0.3072 0.0555 158.67);">Correct selection</span></div><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.2565 0.0265 278.04);"><use xlink:href="#icon-checkbox-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>When you apply a retention period to an object version explicitly, you specify a <code>Retain Until Date</code> for the object version</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-skipped--1NDPn" data-purpose="answer"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.6722 0.0355 279.77);"><use xlink:href="#icon-checkbox-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>When you use bucket default settings, you specify a <code>Retain Until Date</code> for the object version</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--question-related-fields--c3m--"><div class="overall-explanation-pane--overall-explanation--G-hLQ ud-form-group"><label class="ud-heading-md ud-form-label ud-heading-sm" for="form-group--148">Overall explanation</label><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-text-md rt-scaffolding" id="overall-explanation"><p>Correct options:</p>

<p><strong>When you apply a retention period to an object version explicitly, you specify a <code>Retain Until Date</code> for the object version</strong></p>

<p>You can place a retention period on an object version either explicitly or through a bucket default setting. When you apply a retention period to an object version explicitly, you specify a <code>Retain Until Date</code> for the object version. Amazon S3 stores the Retain Until Date setting in the object version's metadata and protects the object version until the retention period expires.</p>

<p><strong>Different versions of a single object can have different retention modes and periods</strong></p>

<p>Like all other Object Lock settings, retention periods apply to individual object versions. Different versions of a single object can have different retention modes and periods.</p>

<p>For example, suppose that you have an object that is 15 days into a 30-day retention period, and you PUT an object into Amazon S3 with the same name and a 60-day retention period. In this case, your PUT succeeds, and Amazon S3 creates a new version of the object with a 60-day retention period. The older version maintains its original retention period and becomes deletable in 15 days.</p>

<p>Incorrect options:</p>

<p><strong>You cannot place a retention period on an object version through a bucket default setting</strong> - You can place a retention period on an object version either explicitly or through a bucket default setting.</p>

<p><strong>When you use bucket default settings, you specify a <code>Retain Until Date</code> for the object version</strong> - When you use bucket default settings, you don't specify a Retain Until Date. Instead, you specify a duration, in either days or years, for which every object version placed in the bucket should be protected.</p>

<p><strong>The bucket default settings will override any explicit retention mode or period you request on an object version</strong> - If your request to place an object version in a bucket contains an explicit retention mode and period, those settings override any bucket default settings for that object version.</p>

<p>Reference:</p>

<p><a href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AmazonS3/latest/dev/object-lock-overview.html">https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AmazonS3/latest/dev/object-lock-overview.html</a></p>

The 'hot data' needs to be both processed and stored quickly in a parallel and distributed fashion. The 'cold data' needs to be kept for reference with quick access for reads and updates at a low cost.</p>

<p>Which of the following AWS services is BEST suited to accelerate the aforementioned chip design process?</p></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--question-result-pane-expanded-content--Og5Vc"><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-skipped--1NDPn" data-purpose="answer"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Amazon FSx for Windows File Server</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-skipped--1NDPn" data-purpose="answer"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.6722 0.0355 279.77);"><use xlink:href="#icon-radio-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>AWS Glue</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-skipped--1NDPn" data-purpose="answer"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.6722 0.0355 279.77);"><use xlink:href="#icon-radio-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Amazon EMR</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-correct--PLOEU" data-purpose="answer"><div><span data-purpose="answer-result-header-user-label" class="result-pane--answer-by-user-label--PSH86 ud-heading-xs" style="background: oklch(0.8101 0.0873 162.22); color: oklch(0.3072 0.0555 158.67);">Correct answer</span></div><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.2565 0.0265 278.04);"><use xlink:href="#icon-radio-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Amazon FSx for Lustre</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--question-related-fields--c3m--"><div class="overall-explanation-pane--overall-explanation--G-hLQ ud-form-group"><label class="ud-heading-md ud-form-label ud-heading-sm" for="form-group--150">Overall explanation</label><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-text-md rt-scaffolding" id="overall-explanation"><p>Correct option:</p>

<p><strong>Amazon FSx for Lustre</strong></p>

<p>Amazon FSx for Lustre makes it easy and cost-effective to launch and run the world’s most popular high-performance file system. It is used for workloads such as machine learning, high-performance computing (HPC), video processing, and financial modeling. The open-source Lustre file system is designed for applications that require fast storage – where you want your storage to keep up with your compute. FSx for Lustre integrates with Amazon S3, making it easy to process data sets with the Lustre file system. When linked to an S3 bucket, an FSx for Lustre file system transparently presents S3 objects as files and allows you to write changed data back to S3.</p>

<p>FSx for Lustre provides the ability to both process the 'hot data' in a parallel and distributed fashion as well as easily store the 'cold data' on Amazon S3. Therefore this option is the BEST fit for the given problem statement.</p>

<p>Incorrect options:</p>

<p><strong>Amazon FSx for Windows File Server</strong> - Amazon FSx for Windows File Server provides fully managed, highly reliable file storage that is accessible over the industry-standard Service Message Block (SMB) protocol.  It is built on Windows Server, delivering a wide range of administrative features such as user quotas, end-user file restore, and Microsoft Active Directory (AD) integration.
FSx for Windows does not allow you to present S3 objects as files and does not allow you to write changed data back to S3. Therefore you cannot reference the "cold data" with quick access for reads and updates at low cost. Hence this option is not correct.</p>

<p><strong>Amazon EMR</strong> - Amazon EMR is the industry-leading cloud big data platform for processing vast amounts of data using open source tools such as Apache Spark, Apache Hive, Apache HBase, Apache Flink, Apache Hudi, and Presto. Amazon EMR uses Hadoop, an open-source framework, to distribute your data and processing across a resizable cluster of Amazon EC2 instances.
EMR does not offer the same storage and processing speed as FSx for Lustre. So it is not the right fit for the given high-performance workflow scenario.</p>

<p><strong>AWS Glue</strong> - AWS Glue is a fully managed extract, transform, and load (ETL) service that makes it easy for customers to prepare and load their data for analytics. AWS Glue job is meant to be used for batch ETL data processing.
AWS Glue does not offer the same storage and processing speed as FSx for Lustre. So it is not the right fit for the given high-performance workflow scenario.</p>

</div></div><div data-purpose="domain-pane" class="domain-pane--domain-pane--Pw9dK"><div class="domain-pane--domain-pane-header--2263m ud-heading-md">Domain</div><div class="ud-text-md">Design High-Performing Architectures</div></div></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--question-result-pane-wrapper--2bGiz"><div class="result-pane--question-result-pane--sIcOh result-pane--accordion-panel--TEJg7"><div class="result-pane--question-header-wrapper--3DCpC"><div class="result-pane--question-header--pTUOx"><span class="result-pane--question-header-collapsed-text--WVdEr"><span class="result-pane--pane-title--f-2kd ud-heading-md"><span data-purpose="question-result-header-status-icon" class="result-pane--answer-status-icon--ebl6C"><span class="result-pane--question-icon-background--AskFJ" data-purpose="question-result-header-status-icon-background" style="background: oklch(0.7905 0.0283 281.19);"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-medium" style="color: oklch(0.7905 0.0283 281.19);"><use xlink:href="#icon-close"></use></svg></span></span><span>Question 9</span><span data-purpose="question-result-header-status-label" style="color: oklch(0.6722 0.0355 279.77);">Skipped</span></span><button type="button" class="ud-btn ud-btn-large ud-btn-ghost ud-btn-text-md ud-btn-icon ud-btn-icon-large"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-medium ud-icon-color-neutral"><use xlink:href="#icon-collapse"></use></svg></button></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="result-pane--question-format--PBvdY ud-text-md rt-scaffolding" id="question-prompt"><p>The IT department at a consulting firm is conducting a training workshop for new developers. As part of an evaluation exercise on Amazon S3, the new developers were asked to identify the invalid storage class lifecycle transitions for objects stored on Amazon S3.</p>

<p>Can you spot the INVALID lifecycle transitions from the options below? (Select two)</p></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--question-result-pane-expanded-content--Og5Vc"><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-skipped--1NDPn" data-purpose="answer"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.6722 0.0355 279.77);"><use xlink:href="#icon-checkbox-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Amazon S3 Standard-IA =&gt; Amazon S3 Intelligent-Tiering</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-correct--PLOEU" data-purpose="answer"><div><span data-purpose="answer-result-header-user-label" class="result-pane--answer-by-user-label--PSH86 ud-heading-xs" style="background: oklch(0.8101 0.0873 162.22); color: oklch(0.3072 0.0555 158.67);">Correct selection</span></div><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.2565 0.0265 278.04);"><use xlink:href="#icon-checkbox-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Amazon S3 Intelligent-Tiering =&gt; Amazon S3 Standard</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-skipped--1NDPn" data-purpose="answer"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.6722 0.0355 279.77);"><use xlink:href="#icon-checkbox-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Amazon S3 Standard-IA =&gt; Amazon S3 One Zone-IA</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-correct--PLOEU" data-purpose="answer"><div><span data-purpose="answer-result-header-user-label" class="result-pane--answer-by-user-label--PSH86 ud-heading-xs" style="background: oklch(0.8101 0.0873 162.22); color: oklch(0.3072 0.0555 158.67);">Correct selection</span></div><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.2565 0.0265 278.04);"><use xlink:href="#icon-checkbox-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Amazon S3 One Zone-IA =&gt; Amazon S3 Standard-IA</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-skipped--1NDPn" data-purpose="answer"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.6722 0.0355 279.77);"><use xlink:href="#icon-checkbox-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Amazon S3 Standard =&gt; Amazon S3 Intelligent-Tiering</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--question-related-fields--c3m--"><div class="overall-explanation-pane--overall-explanation--G-hLQ ud-form-group"><label class="ud-heading-md ud-form-label ud-heading-sm" for="form-group--152">Overall explanation</label><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-text-md rt-scaffolding" id="overall-explanation"><p>Correct options:</p>

<p>As the question wants to know about the INVALID lifecycle transitions, the following options are the correct answers -</p>

<p><strong>Amazon S3 Intelligent-Tiering =&gt; Amazon S3 Standard</strong></p>

<p><strong>Amazon S3 One Zone-IA =&gt; Amazon S3 Standard-IA</strong></p>

<p>Following are the unsupported life cycle transitions for S3 storage classes -
Any storage class to the Amazon S3 Standard storage class.
Any storage class to the Reduced Redundancy storage class.
The Amazon S3 Intelligent-Tiering storage class to the Amazon S3 Standard-IA storage class.
The Amazon S3 One Zone-IA storage class to the Amazon S3 Standard-IA or Amazon S3 Intelligent-Tiering storage classes.</p>

<p>Incorrect options:</p>

<p><strong>Amazon S3 Standard =&gt; Amazon S3 Intelligent-Tiering</strong></p>

<p><strong>Amazon S3 Standard-IA =&gt; Amazon S3 Intelligent-Tiering</strong></p>

<p><strong>Amazon S3 Standard-IA =&gt; Amazon S3 One Zone-IA</strong></p>

<p>Here are the supported life cycle transitions for S3 storage classes -
The S3 Standard storage class to any other storage class.
Any storage class to the S3 Glacier or S3 Glacier Deep Archive storage classes.
The S3 Standard-IA storage class to the S3 Intelligent-Tiering or S3 One Zone-IA storage classes.
The S3 Intelligent-Tiering storage class to the S3 One Zone-IA storage class.
The S3 Glacier storage class to the S3 Glacier Deep Archive storage class.</p>

<p>Amazon S3 supports a waterfall model for transitioning between storage classes, as shown in the diagram below:
<img src="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/images/AmazonS3/latest/userguide/images/lifecycle-transitions-v4.png" style="display: none;"><span class="ud-component--base-components--open-full-size-image"><div class="open-full-size-image--wrapper--R4gIm" data-purpose="open-full-size-image"><img src="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/images/AmazonS3/latest/userguide/images/lifecycle-transitions-v4.png" alt="" loading="eager"><button type="button" class="ud-btn ud-btn-medium ud-btn-link ud-btn-text-sm open-full-size-image--backdrop--Zor3j"><svg aria-label="Larger image" role="img" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-large ud-icon-color-neutral"><use xlink:href="#icon-search"></use></svg></button></div></span>
via - <a href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AmazonS3/latest/userguide/lifecycle-transition-general-considerations.html">https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AmazonS3/latest/userguide/lifecycle-transition-general-considerations.html</a></p>

</div></div><div data-purpose="domain-pane" class="domain-pane--domain-pane--Pw9dK"><div class="domain-pane--domain-pane-header--2263m ud-heading-md">Domain</div><div class="ud-text-md">Design Cost-Optimized Architectures</div></div></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--question-result-pane-wrapper--2bGiz"><div class="result-pane--question-result-pane--sIcOh result-pane--accordion-panel--TEJg7"><div class="result-pane--question-header-wrapper--3DCpC"><div class="result-pane--question-header--pTUOx"><span class="result-pane--question-header-collapsed-text--WVdEr"><span class="result-pane--pane-title--f-2kd ud-heading-md"><span data-purpose="question-result-header-status-icon" class="result-pane--answer-status-icon--ebl6C"><span class="result-pane--question-icon-background--AskFJ" data-purpose="question-result-header-status-icon-background" style="background: oklch(0.7905 0.0283 281.19);"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-medium" style="color: oklch(0.7905 0.0283 281.19);"><use xlink:href="#icon-close"></use></svg></span></span><span>Question 10</span><span data-purpose="question-result-header-status-label" style="color: oklch(0.6722 0.0355 279.77);">Skipped</span></span><button type="button" class="ud-btn ud-btn-large ud-btn-ghost ud-btn-text-md ud-btn-icon ud-btn-icon-large"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-medium ud-icon-color-neutral"><use xlink:href="#icon-collapse"></use></svg></button></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="result-pane--question-format--PBvdY ud-text-md rt-scaffolding" id="question-prompt"><p>A software company has a globally distributed team of developers, that requires secure and compliant access to AWS environments. The company manages multiple AWS accounts under AWS Organizations and uses an on-premises Microsoft Active Directory for user authentication. To simplify access control and identity governance across projects and accounts, the company wants a centrally managed solution that integrates with their existing infrastructure. The solution should require the least amount of ongoing operational management.</p>

<p>Which approach best meets the company’s requirements?</p></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--question-result-pane-expanded-content--Og5Vc"><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-skipped--1NDPn" data-purpose="answer"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.6722 0.0355 279.77);"><use xlink:href="#icon-radio-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Deploy AWS Directory Service for Microsoft Active Directory in AWS. Establish a trust relationship with the on-premises Active Directory. Use IAM roles linked to AD groups to control access to AWS resources</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-skipped--1NDPn" data-purpose="answer"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.6722 0.0355 279.77);"><use xlink:href="#icon-radio-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Use AWS Control Tower to enable account access for developers. Create AWS IAM roles in each member account and manually assign permissions. Instruct developers to assume roles across accounts using the AWS CLI</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-skipped--1NDPn" data-purpose="answer"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.6722 0.0355 279.77);"><use xlink:href="#icon-radio-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Deploy an open-source identity provider (IdP) on Amazon EC2. Synchronize it with the on-premises Active Directory and use SAML to federate access to AWS accounts. Assign IAM roles to federated users based on SAML assertions</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-correct--PLOEU" data-purpose="answer"><div><span data-purpose="answer-result-header-user-label" class="result-pane--answer-by-user-label--PSH86 ud-heading-xs" style="background: oklch(0.8101 0.0873 162.22); color: oklch(0.3072 0.0555 158.67);">Correct answer</span></div><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.2565 0.0265 278.04);"><use xlink:href="#icon-radio-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Use AWS Directory Service AD Connector to connect AWS to the on-premises Active Directory. Integrate AD Connector with AWS IAM Identity Center. Use permission sets to assign access to AWS accounts and resources based on Active Directory group membership</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--question-related-fields--c3m--"><div class="overall-explanation-pane--overall-explanation--G-hLQ ud-form-group"><label class="ud-heading-md ud-form-label ud-heading-sm" for="form-group--154">Overall explanation</label><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-text-md rt-scaffolding" id="overall-explanation"><p>Correct option:</p>

<p><strong>Use AWS Directory Service AD Connector to connect AWS to the on-premises Active Directory. Integrate AD Connector with AWS IAM Identity Center. Use permission sets to assign access to AWS accounts and resources based on Active Directory group membership</strong></p>

<p>This solution provides a centralized, low-maintenance, and scalable identity management solution that integrates seamlessly with the company’s existing on-premises Active Directory. AD Connector acts as a proxy to the on-prem AD, eliminating the need to deploy or manage a separate directory in the cloud. By integrating IAM Identity Center (formerly AWS SSO) with AD Connector, the company can use existing Active Directory group memberships to assign permission sets that define what AWS accounts and resources each user can access. This allows fine-grained, role-based access control across multiple accounts managed by AWS Organizations. IAM Identity Center also provides a single sign-on portal, reducing friction for users while maintaining compliance and security. The entire solution requires minimal operational overhead and scales well with growing teams and AWS accounts.</p>

<p>Incorrect options:</p>

<p><strong>Deploy AWS Directory Service for Microsoft Active Directory in AWS. Establish a trust relationship with the on-premises Active Directory. Use IAM roles linked to AD groups to control access to AWS resources</strong> - While this solution provides centralized identity integration via trust relationships, managing a self-hosted or AWS-managed AD in the cloud adds significant operational overhead. You must maintain the AWS Directory Service instance, monitor trust health, and manage role mappings manually. It does meet the technical need, but it’s less efficient than a fully managed identity federation service such as IAM Identity Center (formerly AWS SSO). It introduces extra cost and maintenance that goes against the requirement for low operational effort.</p>

<p><strong>Deploy an open-source identity provider (IdP) on Amazon EC2. Synchronize it with the on-premises Active Directory and use SAML to federate access to AWS accounts. Assign IAM roles to federated users based on SAML assertions</strong> - While this solution is technically feasible, it introduces significant operational overhead, which contradicts the question’s requirement. Managing an open-source IdP on EC2 - including scaling, patching, high availability, and synchronization with Active Directory is labor-intensive. Although it allows for SAML federation and AWS access, it lacks the native integration, multi-account visibility, and permission set management offered by IAM Identity Center. This approach may suit specific customization needs but fails the test of being simple and low maintenance.</p>

<p><strong>Use AWS Control Tower to enable account access for developers. Create AWS IAM roles in each member account and manually assign permissions. Instruct developers to assume roles across accounts using the AWS CLI</strong> - Although AWS Control Tower helps set up a multi-account environment, this approach involves manual creation and assignment of IAM roles in each account, which is not scalable. Developers must use CLI-based role assumption, and administrators must maintain custom trust policies and permission boundaries. There's no centralized management of access or visibility across accounts, making this solution error-prone and operationally complex compared to using IAM Identity Center with group-based permission sets and automatic propagation across accounts.</p>
