</div></div><div data-purpose="domain-pane" class="domain-pane--domain-pane--Pw9dK"><div class="domain-pane--domain-pane-header--2263m ud-heading-md">Domain</div><div class="ud-text-md">Design High-Performing Architectures</div></div></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--question-result-pane-wrapper--2bGiz"><div class="result-pane--question-result-pane--sIcOh result-pane--accordion-panel--TEJg7"><div class="result-pane--question-header-wrapper--3DCpC"><div class="result-pane--question-header--pTUOx"><span class="result-pane--question-header-collapsed-text--WVdEr"><span class="result-pane--pane-title--f-2kd ud-heading-md"><span data-purpose="question-result-header-status-icon" class="result-pane--answer-status-icon--ebl6C"><span class="result-pane--question-icon-background--AskFJ" data-purpose="question-result-header-status-icon-background" style="background: oklch(0.7905 0.0283 281.19);"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-medium" style="color: oklch(0.7905 0.0283 281.19);"><use xlink:href="#icon-close"></use></svg></span></span><span>Question 26</span><span data-purpose="question-result-header-status-label" style="color: oklch(0.6722 0.0355 279.77);">Skipped</span></span><button type="button" class="ud-btn ud-btn-large ud-btn-ghost ud-btn-text-md ud-btn-icon ud-btn-icon-large"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-medium ud-icon-color-neutral"><use xlink:href="#icon-collapse"></use></svg></button></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="result-pane--question-format--PBvdY ud-text-md rt-scaffolding" id="question-prompt"><p>A video analytics company runs data-intensive batch processing workloads that generate large log files and metadata daily. These files are currently stored in an on-premises NFS-based storage system located in the company's primary data center. However, the storage system is becoming increasingly difficult to scale and is unable to meet the company's growing storage demands. The IT team wants to migrate to a cloud-based storage solution that minimizes costs, retains NFS compatibility, and supports automated tiering of rarely accessed data to lower-cost storage. The team prefers to continue using existing NFS-based tools and protocols for compatibility with their current application stack.</p>

<p>Which solution will meet these requirements MOST cost-effectively?</p></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--question-result-pane-expanded-content--Og5Vc"><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-skipped--1NDPn" data-purpose="answer"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.6722 0.0355 279.77);"><use xlink:href="#icon-radio-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Provision an Amazon Elastic File System (Amazon EFS) file system with the One Zone–IA storage class. Use AWS DataSync to migrate the NFS data to EFS. Configure the application to mount the file system over NFS and activate lifecycle management to tier infrequently accessed files</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-skipped--1NDPn" data-purpose="answer"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.6722 0.0355 279.77);"><use xlink:href="#icon-radio-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Deploy an AWS Storage Gateway Volume Gateway in cached mode. Attach it as a block device to an on-premises file server and mount NFS on top. Store snapshots in Amazon S3 Glacier Deep Archive, and use AWS Backup to manage recovery operations and tiering</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-correct--PLOEU" data-purpose="answer"><div><span data-purpose="answer-result-header-user-label" class="result-pane--answer-by-user-label--PSH86 ud-heading-xs" style="background: oklch(0.8101 0.0873 162.22); color: oklch(0.3072 0.0555 158.67);">Correct answer</span></div><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.2565 0.0265 278.04);"><use xlink:href="#icon-radio-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Deploy an AWS Storage Gateway File Gateway on premises. Configure it to present an NFS-compatible file share to the workloads. Store the uploaded files in Amazon S3, and use S3 Lifecycle policies to automatically transition infrequently accessed objects to lower-cost storage classes</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-skipped--1NDPn" data-purpose="answer"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.6722 0.0355 279.77);"><use xlink:href="#icon-radio-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Use Amazon FSx for Windows File Server to replace the NFS workload. Enable data deduplication and automatic backups. Use Amazon S3 Glacier to move snapshots to a cost-efficient storage tier. Reconfigure the analytics application to access files using SMB protocol</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--question-related-fields--c3m--"><div class="overall-explanation-pane--overall-explanation--G-hLQ ud-form-group"><label class="ud-heading-md ud-form-label ud-heading-sm" for="form-group--186">Overall explanation</label><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-text-md rt-scaffolding" id="overall-explanation"><p>Correct option:</p>

<p><strong>Deploy an AWS Storage Gateway File Gateway on premises. Configure it to present an NFS-compatible file share to the workloads. Store the uploaded files in Amazon S3, and use S3 Lifecycle policies to automatically transition infrequently accessed objects to lower-cost storage classes</strong></p>

<p>This is the most cost-effective and operationally seamless solution. File Gateway presents an NFS-compatible interface to on-premises applications, allowing the existing workloads to write to it as they would to a traditional NFS server. Behind the scenes, the data is stored in Amazon S3, allowing the company to leverage S3's virtually unlimited scalability. With S3 Lifecycle policies, files can be automatically transitioned to low-cost storage classes like S3 Standard-IA or Glacier, further optimizing costs over time. This approach requires minimal changes to applications and eliminates the scalability bottleneck.</p>

<p>How File Gateway Works:
<img src="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/images/filegateway/latest/files3/images/file-gateway-concepts-diagram.png" style="display: none;"><span class="ud-component--base-components--open-full-size-image"><div class="open-full-size-image--wrapper--R4gIm" data-purpose="open-full-size-image"><img src="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/images/filegateway/latest/files3/images/file-gateway-concepts-diagram.png" alt="" loading="eager"><button type="button" class="ud-btn ud-btn-medium ud-btn-link ud-btn-text-sm open-full-size-image--backdrop--Zor3j"><svg aria-label="Larger image" role="img" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-large ud-icon-color-neutral"><use xlink:href="#icon-search"></use></svg></button></div></span>
via - <a href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/filegateway/latest/files3/file-gateway-concepts.html">https://docs.aws.amazon.com/filegateway/latest/files3/file-gateway-concepts.html</a></p>

<p>Incorrect options:</p>

<p><strong>Provision an Amazon Elastic File System (Amazon EFS) file system with the One Zone–IA storage class. Use AWS DataSync to migrate the NFS data to EFS. Configure the application to mount the file system over NFS and activate lifecycle management to tier infrequently accessed files</strong> - Amazon EFS is designed for shared file systems in the cloud, and while it supports NFS and lifecycle management, it is not cost-optimal for hybrid setups where on-prem NFS compatibility is required. Additionally, One Zone-IA stores data in a single Availability Zone, making it less resilient. This solution also assumes a full data migration and reconfiguration of the applications, increasing complexity and operational overhead.</p>

<p><strong>Deploy an AWS Storage Gateway Volume Gateway in cached mode. Attach it as a block device to an on-premises file server and mount NFS on top. Store snapshots in Amazon S3 Glacier Deep Archive, and use AWS Backup to manage recovery operations and tiering</strong> - Volume Gateway provides iSCSI block storage, not file-based access, meaning you would have to mount NFS over a block volume, which is not ideal for compatibility or scalability. Although Volume Gateway can store snapshots in S3 and Glacier, it's not optimized for NFS workloads or direct object access via S3. It also lacks native support for S3 lifecycle tiering, relying instead on backup and snapshot mechanisms.</p>

<p>How Volume Gateway Works:
<img src="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/images/storagegateway/latest/vgw/images/aws-storage-gateway-cached-diagram.png" style="display: none;"><span class="ud-component--base-components--open-full-size-image"><div class="open-full-size-image--wrapper--R4gIm" data-purpose="open-full-size-image"><img src="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/images/storagegateway/latest/vgw/images/aws-storage-gateway-cached-diagram.png" alt="" loading="eager"><button type="button" class="ud-btn ud-btn-medium ud-btn-link ud-btn-text-sm open-full-size-image--backdrop--Zor3j"><svg aria-label="Larger image" role="img" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-large ud-icon-color-neutral"><use xlink:href="#icon-search"></use></svg></button></div></span>
via - <a href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/storagegateway/latest/vgw/StorageGatewayConcepts.html">https://docs.aws.amazon.com/storagegateway/latest/vgw/StorageGatewayConcepts.html</a></p>

<p><strong>Use Amazon FSx for Windows File Server to replace the NFS workload. Enable data deduplication and automatic backups. Use Amazon S3 Glacier to move snapshots to a cost-efficient storage tier. Reconfigure the analytics application to access files using SMB protocol</strong> - Amazon FSx for Windows File Server is intended for Windows-based SMB workloads, not NFS-based environments. It offers useful features like deduplication and backups, but it requires the application to be rewritten or reconfigured to use SMB instead of NFS. Moreover, its integration with Glacier is only applicable to backups and not individual files, and it does not support S3 lifecycle tiering, making it less cost-efficient.</p>

<p><a href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/filegateway/latest/files3/file-gateway-concepts.html">https://docs.aws.amazon.com/filegateway/latest/files3/file-gateway-concepts.html</a></p>

</div></div><div data-purpose="domain-pane" class="domain-pane--domain-pane--Pw9dK"><div class="domain-pane--domain-pane-header--2263m ud-heading-md">Domain</div><div class="ud-text-md">Design Cost-Optimized Architectures</div></div></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--question-result-pane-wrapper--2bGiz"><div class="result-pane--question-result-pane--sIcOh result-pane--accordion-panel--TEJg7"><div class="result-pane--question-header-wrapper--3DCpC"><div class="result-pane--question-header--pTUOx"><span class="result-pane--question-header-collapsed-text--WVdEr"><span class="result-pane--pane-title--f-2kd ud-heading-md"><span data-purpose="question-result-header-status-icon" class="result-pane--answer-status-icon--ebl6C"><span class="result-pane--question-icon-background--AskFJ" data-purpose="question-result-header-status-icon-background" style="background: oklch(0.7905 0.0283 281.19);"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-medium" style="color: oklch(0.7905 0.0283 281.19);"><use xlink:href="#icon-close"></use></svg></span></span><span>Question 27</span><span data-purpose="question-result-header-status-label" style="color: oklch(0.6722 0.0355 279.77);">Skipped</span></span><button type="button" class="ud-btn ud-btn-large ud-btn-ghost ud-btn-text-md ud-btn-icon ud-btn-icon-large"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-medium ud-icon-color-neutral"><use xlink:href="#icon-collapse"></use></svg></button></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="result-pane--question-format--PBvdY ud-text-md rt-scaffolding" id="question-prompt"><p>The engineering team at a Spanish professional football club has built a notification system for its website using Amazon Simple Notification Service (Amazon SNS) notifications which are then handled by an AWS Lambda function for end-user delivery. During the off-season, the notification systems need to handle about 100 requests per second. During the peak football season, the rate touches about 5000 requests per second and it is noticed that a significant number of the notifications are not being delivered to the end-users on the website.</p>

<p>As a solutions architect, which of the following would you suggest as the BEST possible solution to this issue?</p></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--question-result-pane-expanded-content--Og5Vc"><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-skipped--1NDPn" data-purpose="answer"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.6722 0.0355 279.77);"><use xlink:href="#icon-radio-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>The engineering team needs to provision more servers running the Amazon SNS service</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-skipped--1NDPn" data-purpose="answer"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.6722 0.0355 279.77);"><use xlink:href="#icon-radio-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>The engineering team needs to provision more servers running the AWS Lambda service</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-correct--PLOEU" data-purpose="answer"><div><span data-purpose="answer-result-header-user-label" class="result-pane--answer-by-user-label--PSH86 ud-heading-xs" style="background: oklch(0.8101 0.0873 162.22); color: oklch(0.3072 0.0555 158.67);">Correct answer</span></div><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.2565 0.0265 278.04);"><use xlink:href="#icon-radio-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Amazon SNS message deliveries to AWS Lambda have crossed the account concurrency quota for AWS Lambda, so the team needs to contact AWS support to raise the account limit</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-skipped--1NDPn" data-purpose="answer"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.6722 0.0355 279.77);"><use xlink:href="#icon-radio-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Amazon SNS has hit a scalability limit, so the team needs to contact AWS support to raise the account limit</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--question-related-fields--c3m--"><div class="overall-explanation-pane--overall-explanation--G-hLQ ud-form-group"><label class="ud-heading-md ud-form-label ud-heading-sm" for="form-group--188">Overall explanation</label><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-text-md rt-scaffolding" id="overall-explanation"><p>Correct option:</p>

<p><strong>Amazon SNS message deliveries to AWS Lambda have crossed the account concurrency quota for AWS Lambda, so the team needs to contact AWS support to raise the account limit</strong></p>

<p>Amazon Simple Notification Service (Amazon SNS) is a highly available, durable, secure, fully managed pub/sub messaging service that enables you to decouple microservices, distributed systems, and serverless applications.</p>

<p>How Amazon SNS Works:
<img src="https://d1.awsstatic.com/product-marketing/SNS/product-page-diagram_SNS_how-it-works_1.53a464980bf0d5a868b141e9a8b2acf12abc503f.png" style="display: none;"><span class="ud-component--base-components--open-full-size-image"><div class="open-full-size-image--wrapper--R4gIm" data-purpose="open-full-size-image"><img src="https://d1.awsstatic.com/product-marketing/SNS/product-page-diagram_SNS_how-it-works_1.53a464980bf0d5a868b141e9a8b2acf12abc503f.png" alt="" loading="eager"><button type="button" class="ud-btn ud-btn-medium ud-btn-link ud-btn-text-sm open-full-size-image--backdrop--Zor3j"><svg aria-label="Larger image" role="img" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-large ud-icon-color-neutral"><use xlink:href="#icon-search"></use></svg></button></div></span>
via - <a href="https://aws.amazon.com/sns/">https://aws.amazon.com/sns/</a></p>

<p>With AWS Lambda, you can run code without provisioning or managing servers. You pay only for the compute time that you consume—there’s no charge when your code isn’t running.</p>

<p>AWS Lambda currently supports 1000 concurrent executions per AWS account per region. If your Amazon SNS message deliveries to AWS Lambda contribute to crossing these concurrency quotas, your Amazon SNS message deliveries will be throttled. You need to contact AWS support to raise the account limit. Therefore this option is correct.</p>

<p>Incorrect options:</p>

<p><strong>Amazon SNS has hit a scalability limit, so the team needs to contact AWS support to raise the account limit</strong> - Amazon SNS leverages the proven AWS cloud to dynamically scale with your application. You don't need to contact AWS support, as SNS is a fully managed service, taking care of the heavy lifting related to capacity planning, provisioning, monitoring, and patching. Therefore, this option is incorrect.</p>

<p><strong>The engineering team needs to provision more servers running the Amazon SNS service</strong></p>

<p><strong>The engineering team needs to provision more servers running the AWS Lambda service</strong></p>

<p>As both AWS Lambda and Amazon SNS are serverless and fully managed services, the engineering team cannot provision more servers. Both of these options are incorrect.</p>

<p>References:</p>

<p><a href="https://aws.amazon.com/sns/">https://aws.amazon.com/sns/</a></p>

</div></div><div data-purpose="domain-pane" class="domain-pane--domain-pane--Pw9dK"><div class="domain-pane--domain-pane-header--2263m ud-heading-md">Domain</div><div class="ud-text-md">Design Resilient Architectures</div></div></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--question-result-pane-wrapper--2bGiz"><div class="result-pane--question-result-pane--sIcOh result-pane--accordion-panel--TEJg7"><div class="result-pane--question-header-wrapper--3DCpC"><div class="result-pane--question-header--pTUOx"><span class="result-pane--question-header-collapsed-text--WVdEr"><span class="result-pane--pane-title--f-2kd ud-heading-md"><span data-purpose="question-result-header-status-icon" class="result-pane--answer-status-icon--ebl6C"><span class="result-pane--question-icon-background--AskFJ" data-purpose="question-result-header-status-icon-background" style="background: oklch(0.7905 0.0283 281.19);"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-medium" style="color: oklch(0.7905 0.0283 281.19);"><use xlink:href="#icon-close"></use></svg></span></span><span>Question 28</span><span data-purpose="question-result-header-status-label" style="color: oklch(0.6722 0.0355 279.77);">Skipped</span></span><button type="button" class="ud-btn ud-btn-large ud-btn-ghost ud-btn-text-md ud-btn-icon ud-btn-icon-large"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-medium ud-icon-color-neutral"><use xlink:href="#icon-collapse"></use></svg></button></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="result-pane--question-format--PBvdY ud-text-md rt-scaffolding" id="question-prompt"><p>A software engineering intern at an e-commerce company is documenting the process flow to provision Amazon EC2 instances via the Amazon EC2 API. These instances are to be used for an internal application that processes Human Resources payroll data. He wants to highlight those volume types that cannot be used as a boot volume.</p>

<p>Can you help the intern by identifying those storage volume types that CANNOT be used as boot volumes while creating the instances? (Select two)</p></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--question-result-pane-expanded-content--Og5Vc"><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-skipped--1NDPn" data-purpose="answer"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.6722 0.0355 279.77);"><use xlink:href="#icon-checkbox-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>General Purpose Solid State Drive (gp2)</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-correct--PLOEU" data-purpose="answer"><div><span data-purpose="answer-result-header-user-label" class="result-pane--answer-by-user-label--PSH86 ud-heading-xs" style="background: oklch(0.8101 0.0873 162.22); color: oklch(0.3072 0.0555 158.67);">Correct selection</span></div><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.2565 0.0265 278.04);"><use xlink:href="#icon-checkbox-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Throughput Optimized Hard disk drive (st1)</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-skipped--1NDPn" data-purpose="answer"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.6722 0.0355 279.77);"><use xlink:href="#icon-checkbox-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Instance Store</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-correct--PLOEU" data-purpose="answer"><div><span data-purpose="answer-result-header-user-label" class="result-pane--answer-by-user-label--PSH86 ud-heading-xs" style="background: oklch(0.8101 0.0873 162.22); color: oklch(0.3072 0.0555 158.67);">Correct selection</span></div><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.2565 0.0265 278.04);"><use xlink:href="#icon-checkbox-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Cold Hard disk drive (sc1)</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-skipped--1NDPn" data-purpose="answer"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.6722 0.0355 279.77);"><use xlink:href="#icon-checkbox-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Provisioned IOPS Solid state drive (io1)</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--question-related-fields--c3m--"><div class="overall-explanation-pane--overall-explanation--G-hLQ ud-form-group"><label class="ud-heading-md ud-form-label ud-heading-sm" for="form-group--190">Overall explanation</label><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-text-md rt-scaffolding" id="overall-explanation"><p>Correct options:</p>

<p><strong>Throughput Optimized Hard disk drive (st1)</strong></p>

<p><strong>Cold Hard disk drive (sc1)</strong></p>

<p>The Amazon EBS volume types fall into two categories:</p>

<p>Solid state drive (SSD) backed volumes optimized for transactional workloads involving frequent read/write operations with small I/O size, where the dominant performance attribute is IOPS.</p>

<p>Hard disk drive (HDD) backed volumes optimized for large streaming workloads where throughput (measured in MiB/s) is a better performance measure than IOPS.</p>

<p>Throughput Optimized HDD (st1) and Cold HDD (sc1) volume types CANNOT be used as a boot volume, so these two options are correct.</p>

<p>Please see this detailed overview of the volume types for Amazon EBS volumes.
<img src="https://assets-pt.media.datacumulus.com/aws-saa-pt/assets/pt1-q43-i1.jpg" style="display: none;"><span class="ud-component--base-components--open-full-size-image"><div class="open-full-size-image--wrapper--R4gIm" data-purpose="open-full-size-image"><img src="https://assets-pt.media.datacumulus.com/aws-saa-pt/assets/pt1-q43-i1.jpg" alt="" loading="eager"><button type="button" class="ud-btn ud-btn-medium ud-btn-link ud-btn-text-sm open-full-size-image--backdrop--Zor3j"><svg aria-label="Larger image" role="img" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-large ud-icon-color-neutral"><use xlink:href="#icon-search"></use></svg></button></div></span>
via - <a href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AWSEC2/latest/UserGuide/ebs-volume-types.html">https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AWSEC2/latest/UserGuide/ebs-volume-types.html</a></p>

<p>Incorrect options:</p>

<p><strong>General Purpose Solid State Drive (gp2)</strong></p>

<p><strong>Provisioned IOPS Solid state drive (io1)</strong></p>

<p><strong>Instance Store</strong></p>

<p>General Purpose SSD (gp2), Provisioned IOPS SSD (io1), and Instance Store can be used as a boot volume.</p>

<p>References:</p>

<p><a href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AWSEC2/latest/UserGuide/ebs-volume-types.html">https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AWSEC2/latest/UserGuide/ebs-volume-types.html</a></p>

</div></div><div data-purpose="domain-pane" class="domain-pane--domain-pane--Pw9dK"><div class="domain-pane--domain-pane-header--2263m ud-heading-md">Domain</div><div class="ud-text-md">Design High-Performing Architectures</div></div></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--question-result-pane-wrapper--2bGiz"><div class="result-pane--question-result-pane--sIcOh result-pane--accordion-panel--TEJg7"><div class="result-pane--question-header-wrapper--3DCpC"><div class="result-pane--question-header--pTUOx"><span class="result-pane--question-header-collapsed-text--WVdEr"><span class="result-pane--pane-title--f-2kd ud-heading-md"><span data-purpose="question-result-header-status-icon" class="result-pane--answer-status-icon--ebl6C"><span class="result-pane--question-icon-background--AskFJ" data-purpose="question-result-header-status-icon-background" style="background: oklch(0.7905 0.0283 281.19);"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-medium" style="color: oklch(0.7905 0.0283 281.19);"><use xlink:href="#icon-close"></use></svg></span></span><span>Question 29</span><span data-purpose="question-result-header-status-label" style="color: oklch(0.6722 0.0355 279.77);">Skipped</span></span><button type="button" class="ud-btn ud-btn-large ud-btn-ghost ud-btn-text-md ud-btn-icon ud-btn-icon-large"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-medium ud-icon-color-neutral"><use xlink:href="#icon-collapse"></use></svg></button></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="result-pane--question-format--PBvdY ud-text-md rt-scaffolding" id="question-prompt"><p>A leading carmaker would like to build a new car-as-a-sensor service by leveraging fully serverless components that are provisioned and managed automatically by AWS. The development team at the carmaker does not want an option that requires the capacity to be manually provisioned, as it does not want to respond manually to changing volumes of sensor data.</p>

<p>Given these constraints, which of the following solutions is the BEST fit to develop this car-as-a-sensor service?</p></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--question-result-pane-expanded-content--Og5Vc"><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-skipped--1NDPn" data-purpose="answer"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Ingest the sensor data in Amazon Kinesis Data Firehose, which directly writes the data into an auto-scaled Amazon DynamoDB table for downstream processing</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-skipped--1NDPn" data-purpose="answer"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.6722 0.0355 279.77);"><use xlink:href="#icon-radio-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Ingest the sensor data in an Amazon Simple Queue Service (Amazon SQS) standard queue, which is polled by an application running on an Amazon EC2 instance and the data is written into an auto-scaled Amazon DynamoDB table for downstream processing</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-correct--PLOEU" data-purpose="answer"><div><span data-purpose="answer-result-header-user-label" class="result-pane--answer-by-user-label--PSH86 ud-heading-xs" style="background: oklch(0.8101 0.0873 162.22); color: oklch(0.3072 0.0555 158.67);">Correct answer</span></div><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.2565 0.0265 278.04);"><use xlink:href="#icon-radio-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Ingest the sensor data in an Amazon Simple Queue Service (Amazon SQS) standard queue, which is polled by an AWS Lambda function in batches and the data is written into an auto-scaled Amazon DynamoDB table for downstream processing</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-skipped--1NDPn" data-purpose="answer"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.6722 0.0355 279.77);"><use xlink:href="#icon-radio-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Ingest the sensor data in Amazon Kinesis Data Streams, which is polled by an application running on an Amazon EC2 instance and the data is written into an auto-scaled Amazon DynamoDB table for downstream processing</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--question-related-fields--c3m--"><div class="overall-explanation-pane--overall-explanation--G-hLQ ud-form-group"><label class="ud-heading-md ud-form-label ud-heading-sm" for="form-group--192">Overall explanation</label><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-text-md rt-scaffolding" id="overall-explanation"><p>Correct option:</p>

<p><strong>Ingest the sensor data in an Amazon Simple Queue Service (Amazon SQS) standard queue, which is polled by an AWS Lambda function in batches and the data is written into an auto-scaled Amazon DynamoDB table for downstream processing</strong></p>

<p>AWS Lambda lets you run code without provisioning or managing servers. You pay only for the compute time you consume. Amazon Simple Queue Service (SQS) is a fully managed message queuing service that enables you to decouple and scale microservices, distributed systems, and serverless applications. SQS offers two types of message queues. Standard queues offer maximum throughput, best-effort ordering, and at-least-once delivery. SQS FIFO queues are designed to guarantee that messages are processed exactly once, in the exact order that they are sent.</p>

<p>AWS manages all ongoing operations and underlying infrastructure needed to provide a highly available and scalable message queuing service. With SQS, there is no upfront cost, no need to acquire, install, and configure messaging software, and no time-consuming build-out and maintenance of supporting infrastructure. SQS queues are dynamically created and scale automatically so you can build and grow applications quickly and efficiently.</p>

<p>As there is no need to manually provision the capacity, so this is the correct option.</p>

<p>Incorrect options:</p>

<p><strong>Ingest the sensor data in Amazon Kinesis Data Firehose, which directly writes the data into an auto-scaled Amazon DynamoDB table for downstream processing</strong> -Amazon Kinesis Data Firehose is a fully managed service for delivering real-time streaming data to destinations such as Amazon Simple Storage Service (Amazon S3), Amazon Redshift, Amazon OpenSearch Service, Splunk, and any custom HTTP endpoint or HTTP endpoints owned by supported third-party service providers, including Datadog, Dynatrace, LogicMonitor, MongoDB, New Relic, and Sumo Logic.</p>

<p>Firehose cannot directly write into a DynamoDB table, so this option is incorrect.</p>

<p><strong>Ingest the sensor data in an Amazon Simple Queue Service (Amazon SQS) standard queue, which is polled by an application running on an Amazon EC2 instance and the data is written into an auto-scaled Amazon DynamoDB table for downstream processing</strong></p>

<p><strong>Ingest the sensor data in Amazon Kinesis Data Streams, which is polled by an application running on an Amazon EC2 instance and the data is written into an auto-scaled Amazon DynamoDB table for downstream processing</strong></p>

<p>Using an application on an Amazon EC2 instance is ruled out as the carmaker wants to use fully serverless components. So both these options are incorrect.</p>

<p>References:</p>

<p><a href="https://aws.amazon.com/sqs/">https://aws.amazon.com/sqs/</a></p>

<p><a href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/lambda/latest/dg/with-kinesis.html">https://docs.aws.amazon.com/lambda/latest/dg/with-kinesis.html</a></p>

<p><a href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/lambda/latest/dg/with-sqs.html">https://docs.aws.amazon.com/lambda/latest/dg/with-sqs.html</a></p>

<p><a href="https://aws.amazon.com/kinesis/data-streams/faqs/">https://aws.amazon.com/kinesis/data-streams/faqs/</a></p>

The team wants to route traffic to multiple back-end services based on the URL path of the HTTP header. So it wants requests for https://www.example.com/orders to go to a specific microservice and requests for https://www.example.com/products to go to another microservice.</p>

<p>Which of the following features of Application Load Balancers can be used for this use-case?</p></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--question-result-pane-expanded-content--Og5Vc"><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-skipped--1NDPn" data-purpose="answer"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.6722 0.0355 279.77);"><use xlink:href="#icon-radio-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Host-based Routing</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-correct--PLOEU" data-purpose="answer"><div><span data-purpose="answer-result-header-user-label" class="result-pane--answer-by-user-label--PSH86 ud-heading-xs" style="background: oklch(0.8101 0.0873 162.22); color: oklch(0.3072 0.0555 158.67);">Correct answer</span></div><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.2565 0.0265 278.04);"><use xlink:href="#icon-radio-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Path-based Routing</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-skipped--1NDPn" data-purpose="answer"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.6722 0.0355 279.77);"><use xlink:href="#icon-radio-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>HTTP header-based routing</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-skipped--1NDPn" data-purpose="answer"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.6722 0.0355 279.77);"><use xlink:href="#icon-radio-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Query string parameter-based routing</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--question-related-fields--c3m--"><div class="overall-explanation-pane--overall-explanation--G-hLQ ud-form-group"><label class="ud-heading-md ud-form-label ud-heading-sm" for="form-group--194">Overall explanation</label><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-text-md rt-scaffolding" id="overall-explanation"><p>Correct option:</p>

<p><strong>Path-based Routing</strong></p>

<p>Elastic Load Balancing automatically distributes incoming application traffic across multiple targets, such as Amazon EC2 instances, containers, IP addresses, and AWS Lambda functions.</p>

<p>If your application is composed of several individual services, an Application Load Balancer can route a request to a service based on the content of the request. Here are the different types -</p>

<p>Host-based Routing:</p>

<p>You can route a client request based on the Host field of the HTTP header allowing you to route to multiple domains from the same load balancer.</p>

<p>Path-based Routing:</p>

<p>You can route a client request based on the URL path of the HTTP header.</p>

<p>HTTP header-based routing:</p>

<p>You can route a client request based on the value of any standard or custom HTTP header.</p>

<p>HTTP method-based routing:</p>

<p>You can route a client request based on any standard or custom HTTP method.</p>

<p>Query string parameter-based routing:</p>

<p>You can route a client request based on the query string or query parameters.</p>

<p>Source IP address CIDR-based routing:</p>

<p>You can route a client request based on source IP address CIDR from where the request originates.</p>

<p>Path-based Routing Overview:</p>

<p>You can use path conditions to define rules that route requests based on the URL in the request (also known as path-based routing).</p>

<p>The path pattern is applied only to the path of the URL, not to its query parameters.
<img src="https://assets-pt.media.datacumulus.com/aws-saa-pt/assets/pt1-q48-i1.jpg" style="display: none;"><span class="ud-component--base-components--open-full-size-image"><div class="open-full-size-image--wrapper--R4gIm" data-purpose="open-full-size-image"><img src="https://assets-pt.media.datacumulus.com/aws-saa-pt/assets/pt1-q48-i1.jpg" alt="" loading="eager"><button type="button" class="ud-btn ud-btn-medium ud-btn-link ud-btn-text-sm open-full-size-image--backdrop--Zor3j"><svg aria-label="Larger image" role="img" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-large ud-icon-color-neutral"><use xlink:href="#icon-search"></use></svg></button></div></span>
via - <a href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/elasticloadbalancing/latest/application/load-balancer-listeners.html#path-conditions">https://docs.aws.amazon.com/elasticloadbalancing/latest/application/load-balancer-listeners.html#path-conditions</a></p>

<p>Incorrect options:</p>

<p><strong>Query string parameter-based routing</strong></p>

<p><strong>HTTP header-based routing</strong></p>

<p><strong>Host-based Routing</strong></p>

<p>As mentioned earlier in the explanation, none of these three types of routing support requests based on the URL path of the HTTP header. Hence these three are incorrect.</p>

<p>Reference:</p>

<p><a href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/elasticloadbalancing/latest/application/load-balancer-listeners.html">https://docs.aws.amazon.com/elasticloadbalancing/latest/application/load-balancer-listeners.html</a></p>
</div></div><div data-purpose="domain-pane" class="domain-pane--domain-pane--Pw9dK"><div class="domain-pane--domain-pane-header--2263m ud-heading-md">Domain</div><div class="ud-text-md">Design Resilient Architectures</div></div></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--question-result-pane-wrapper--2bGiz"><div class="result-pane--question-result-pane--sIcOh result-pane--accordion-panel--TEJg7"><div class="result-pane--question-header-wrapper--3DCpC"><div class="result-pane--question-header--pTUOx"><span class="result-pane--question-header-collapsed-text--WVdEr"><span class="result-pane--pane-title--f-2kd ud-heading-md"><span data-purpose="question-result-header-status-icon" class="result-pane--answer-status-icon--ebl6C"><span class="result-pane--question-icon-background--AskFJ" data-purpose="question-result-header-status-icon-background" style="background: oklch(0.7905 0.0283 281.19);"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-medium" style="color: oklch(0.7905 0.0283 281.19);"><use xlink:href="#icon-close"></use></svg></span></span><span>Question 31</span><span data-purpose="question-result-header-status-label" style="color: oklch(0.6722 0.0355 279.77);">Skipped</span></span><button type="button" class="ud-btn ud-btn-large ud-btn-ghost ud-btn-text-md ud-btn-icon ud-btn-icon-large"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-medium ud-icon-color-neutral"><use xlink:href="#icon-collapse"></use></svg></button></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="result-pane--question-format--PBvdY ud-text-md rt-scaffolding" id="question-prompt"><p>A government agency is developing a online application to assist users in submitting permit requests through a web-based interface. The system architecture consists of a front-end web application tier and a background processing tier that handles the validation and submission of the forms. The application is expected to see high traffic and it must ensure that every submitted request is processed exactly once, with no loss of data.</p>

<p>Which design choice best satisfies these requirements?</p></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--question-result-pane-expanded-content--Og5Vc"><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-skipped--1NDPn" data-purpose="answer"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.6722 0.0355 279.77);"><use xlink:href="#icon-radio-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Leverage Amazon API Gateway to pass the form submissions to AWS Lambda for processing in real time</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-correct--PLOEU" data-purpose="answer"><div><span data-purpose="answer-result-header-user-label" class="result-pane--answer-by-user-label--PSH86 ud-heading-xs" style="background: oklch(0.8101 0.0873 162.22); color: oklch(0.3072 0.0555 158.67);">Correct answer</span></div><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.2565 0.0265 278.04);"><use xlink:href="#icon-radio-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Implement an Amazon SQS FIFO queue to reliably buffer and deliver form submissions from the web application layer to the processing tier</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-skipped--1NDPn" data-purpose="answer"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.6722 0.0355 279.77);"><use xlink:href="#icon-radio-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Leverage Amazon EventBridge to send events from the web application to the processing tier for asynchronous form handling</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-skipped--1NDPn" data-purpose="answer"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.6722 0.0355 279.77);"><use xlink:href="#icon-radio-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Implement an Amazon SQS standard queue to reliably buffer and deliver form submissions from the web application layer to the processing tier</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--question-related-fields--c3m--"><div class="overall-explanation-pane--overall-explanation--G-hLQ ud-form-group"><label class="ud-heading-md ud-form-label ud-heading-sm" for="form-group--196">Overall explanation</label><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-text-md rt-scaffolding" id="overall-explanation"><p>Correct option:</p>

<p><strong>Implement an Amazon SQS FIFO queue to reliably buffer and deliver form submissions from the web application layer to the processing tier</strong></p>

<p>SQS FIFO (First-In-First-Out) queues are designed for exactly-once message processing with order preservation. They prevent duplicate deliveries, making them ideal for transactional workflows such as registration or permit submissions. FIFO queues guarantee that each message is delivered and processed once and only once, which satisfies the application’s reliability and data integrity requirements.</p>

<p>Incorrect options:</p>

<p><strong>Implement an Amazon SQS standard queue to reliably buffer and deliver form submissions from the web application layer to the processing tier</strong> - The option to leverage an Amazon Simple Queue Service (Amazon SQS) standard queue between the web and processing tiers is incorrect for this use case because SQS standard queues do not guarantee exactly-once message delivery. Instead, they provide at-least-once delivery and best-effort ordering. In the context of form submissions or permit requests—where each submission must be processed exactly once and in the correct order—standard queues introduce the risk of duplicate messages or out-of-order processing</p>

<p><strong>Leverage Amazon EventBridge to send events from the web application to the processing tier for asynchronous form handling</strong> - Amazon EventBridge is a powerful event bus that enables loosely coupled architectures and event-driven applications. However, it does not guarantee exactly-once delivery. Instead, EventBridge provides at-least-once delivery semantics, which means events can be delivered more than once in certain failure scenarios. So, the key shortcomings for this use case are - no built-in ordering of events and possible duplicate event delivery.</p>

<p><strong>Leverage Amazon API Gateway to pass the form submissions to AWS Lambda for processing in real time</strong> - While API Gateway with Lambda is effective for real-time synchronous processing, it does not inherently offer decoupling between tiers or a durable queue. It also lacks native support for guaranteed exactly-once processing across asynchronous workloads.</p>

<p>References:</p>

<p><a href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AWSSimpleQueueService/latest/SQSDeveloperGuide/welcome.html">https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AWSSimpleQueueService/latest/SQSDeveloperGuide/welcome.html</a></p>

<p><a href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AWSSimpleQueueService/latest/SQSDeveloperGuide/sqs-fifo-queues.html">https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AWSSimpleQueueService/latest/SQSDeveloperGuide/sqs-fifo-queues.html</a></p>

<p><a href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AWSSimpleQueueService/latest/SQSDeveloperGuide/standard-queues.html">https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AWSSimpleQueueService/latest/SQSDeveloperGuide/standard-queues.html</a></p>
</div></div><div data-purpose="domain-pane" class="domain-pane--domain-pane--Pw9dK"><div class="domain-pane--domain-pane-header--2263m ud-heading-md">Domain</div><div class="ud-text-md">Design Resilient Architectures</div></div></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--question-result-pane-wrapper--2bGiz"><div class="result-pane--question-result-pane--sIcOh result-pane--accordion-panel--TEJg7"><div class="result-pane--question-header-wrapper--3DCpC"><div class="result-pane--question-header--pTUOx"><span class="result-pane--question-header-collapsed-text--WVdEr"><span class="result-pane--pane-title--f-2kd ud-heading-md"><span data-purpose="question-result-header-status-icon" class="result-pane--answer-status-icon--ebl6C"><span class="result-pane--question-icon-background--AskFJ" data-purpose="question-result-header-status-icon-background" style="background: oklch(0.7905 0.0283 281.19);"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-medium" style="color: oklch(0.7905 0.0283 281.19);"><use xlink:href="#icon-close"></use></svg></span></span><span>Question 32</span><span data-purpose="question-result-header-status-label" style="color: oklch(0.6722 0.0355 279.77);">Skipped</span></span><button type="button" class="ud-btn ud-btn-large ud-btn-ghost ud-btn-text-md ud-btn-icon ud-btn-icon-large"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-medium ud-icon-color-neutral"><use xlink:href="#icon-collapse"></use></svg></button></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="result-pane--question-format--PBvdY ud-text-md rt-scaffolding" id="question-prompt"><p>A company runs a data processing workflow that takes about 60 minutes to complete. The workflow can withstand disruptions and it can be started and stopped multiple times.</p>

<p>Which is the most cost-effective solution to build a solution for the workflow?</p></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--question-result-pane-expanded-content--Og5Vc"><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-skipped--1NDPn" data-purpose="answer"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.6722 0.0355 279.77);"><use xlink:href="#icon-radio-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Use AWS Lambda function to run the workflow processes</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-skipped--1NDPn" data-purpose="answer"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.6722 0.0355 279.77);"><use xlink:href="#icon-radio-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Use Amazon EC2 on-demand instances to run the workflow processes</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-skipped--1NDPn" data-purpose="answer"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.6722 0.0355 279.77);"><use xlink:href="#icon-radio-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Use Amazon EC2 reserved instances to run the workflow processes</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-correct--PLOEU" data-purpose="answer"><div><span data-purpose="answer-result-header-user-label" class="result-pane--answer-by-user-label--PSH86 ud-heading-xs" style="background: oklch(0.8101 0.0873 162.22); color: oklch(0.3072 0.0555 158.67);">Correct answer</span></div><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.2565 0.0265 278.04);"><use xlink:href="#icon-radio-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Use Amazon EC2 spot instances to run the workflow processes</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--question-related-fields--c3m--"><div class="overall-explanation-pane--overall-explanation--G-hLQ ud-form-group"><label class="ud-heading-md ud-form-label ud-heading-sm" for="form-group--198">Overall explanation</label><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-text-md rt-scaffolding" id="overall-explanation"><p>Correct option:</p>

<p><strong>Use Amazon EC2 spot instances to run the workflow processes</strong></p>

<p>Amazon EC2 instance types:
<img src="https://assets-pt.media.datacumulus.com/aws-saa-pt/assets/pt1-q21-i1.jpg" style="display: none;"><span class="ud-component--base-components--open-full-size-image"><div class="open-full-size-image--wrapper--R4gIm" data-purpose="open-full-size-image"><img src="https://assets-pt.media.datacumulus.com/aws-saa-pt/assets/pt1-q21-i1.jpg" alt="" loading="eager"><button type="button" class="ud-btn ud-btn-medium ud-btn-link ud-btn-text-sm open-full-size-image--backdrop--Zor3j"><svg aria-label="Larger image" role="img" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-large ud-icon-color-neutral"><use xlink:href="#icon-search"></use></svg></button></div></span>
via - <a href="https://aws.amazon.com/ec2/pricing/">https://aws.amazon.com/ec2/pricing/</a></p>

<p>Amazon EC2 Spot instances allow you to request spare Amazon EC2 computing capacity for up to 90% off the On-Demand price.</p>

<p>Spot instances are recommended for:</p>

<p>Applications that have flexible start and end times
Applications that are feasible only at very low compute prices
Users with urgent computing needs for large amounts of additional capacity</p>

<p>For the given use case, spot instances offer the most cost-effective solution as the workflow can withstand disruptions and can be started and stopped multiple times.</p>

<p>For example, considering a process that runs for an hour and needs about 1024 MB of memory, spot instance pricing for a t2.micro instance (having 1024 MB of RAM) is $0.0035 per hour.</p>

<p>Spot instance pricing:
<img src="https://assets-pt.media.datacumulus.com/aws-saa-pt/assets/pt1-q21-i2.jpg" style="display: none;"><span class="ud-component--base-components--open-full-size-image"><div class="open-full-size-image--wrapper--R4gIm" data-purpose="open-full-size-image"><img src="https://assets-pt.media.datacumulus.com/aws-saa-pt/assets/pt1-q21-i2.jpg" alt="" loading="eager"><button type="button" class="ud-btn ud-btn-medium ud-btn-link ud-btn-text-sm open-full-size-image--backdrop--Zor3j"><svg aria-label="Larger image" role="img" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-large ud-icon-color-neutral"><use xlink:href="#icon-search"></use></svg></button></div></span>
via - <a href="https://aws.amazon.com/ec2/spot/pricing/">https://aws.amazon.com/ec2/spot/pricing/</a></p>

<p>Contrast this with the pricing of a Lambda function (having 1024 MB of allocated memory), which comes out to $0.0000000167 per 1ms or $0.06 per hour ($0.0000000167 * 1000 * 60  * 60 per hour).</p>

<p>AWS Lambda function pricing:
<img src="https://assets-pt.media.datacumulus.com/aws-saa-pt/assets/pt1-q21-i3.jpg" style="display: none;"><span class="ud-component--base-components--open-full-size-image"><div class="open-full-size-image--wrapper--R4gIm" data-purpose="open-full-size-image"><img src="https://assets-pt.media.datacumulus.com/aws-saa-pt/assets/pt1-q21-i3.jpg" alt="" loading="eager"><button type="button" class="ud-btn ud-btn-medium ud-btn-link ud-btn-text-sm open-full-size-image--backdrop--Zor3j"><svg aria-label="Larger image" role="img" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-large ud-icon-color-neutral"><use xlink:href="#icon-search"></use></svg></button></div></span>
via - <a href="https://aws.amazon.com/lambda/pricing/">https://aws.amazon.com/lambda/pricing/</a></p>

<p>Thus, a spot instance turns out to be about 20 times cost effective than a Lambda function to meet the requirements of the given use case.</p>

<p>Incorrect options:</p>

<p><strong>Use AWS Lambda function to run the workflow processes</strong> - As mentioned in the explanation above, a Lambda function turns out to be 20 times more expensive than a spot instance to meet the workflow requirements of the given use case, so this option is incorrect. You should also note that the maximum execution time of a Lambda function is 15 minutes, so the workflow process would be disrupted for sure. On the other hand, it is certainly possible that the workflow process can be completed in a single run on the spot instance (the average frequency of stop instance interruption across all Regions and instance types is &lt;10%).</p>

<p><strong>Use Amazon EC2 on-demand instances to run the workflow processes</strong></p>

<p><strong>Use Amazon EC2 reserved instances to run the workflow processes</strong></p>

<p>You should note that both on-demand and reserved instances are more expensive than spot instances. In addition, reserved instances have a term of 1 year or 3 years, so they are not suited for the given workflow. Therefore, both these options are incorrect.</p>

<p>References:</p>

<p><a href="https://aws.amazon.com/ec2/pricing/">https://aws.amazon.com/ec2/pricing/</a></p>

<p><a href="https://aws.amazon.com/ec2/spot/pricing/">https://aws.amazon.com/ec2/spot/pricing/</a></p>

</div></div><div data-purpose="domain-pane" class="domain-pane--domain-pane--Pw9dK"><div class="domain-pane--domain-pane-header--2263m ud-heading-md">Domain</div><div class="ud-text-md">Design Cost-Optimized Architectures</div></div></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--question-result-pane-wrapper--2bGiz"><div class="result-pane--question-result-pane--sIcOh result-pane--accordion-panel--TEJg7"><div class="result-pane--question-header-wrapper--3DCpC"><div class="result-pane--question-header--pTUOx"><span class="result-pane--question-header-collapsed-text--WVdEr"><span class="result-pane--pane-title--f-2kd ud-heading-md"><span data-purpose="question-result-header-status-icon" class="result-pane--answer-status-icon--ebl6C"><span class="result-pane--question-icon-background--AskFJ" data-purpose="question-result-header-status-icon-background" style="background: oklch(0.7905 0.0283 281.19);"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-medium" style="color: oklch(0.7905 0.0283 281.19);"><use xlink:href="#icon-close"></use></svg></span></span><span>Question 33</span><span data-purpose="question-result-header-status-label" style="color: oklch(0.6722 0.0355 279.77);">Skipped</span></span><button type="button" class="ud-btn ud-btn-large ud-btn-ghost ud-btn-text-md ud-btn-icon ud-btn-icon-large"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-medium ud-icon-color-neutral"><use xlink:href="#icon-collapse"></use></svg></button></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="result-pane--question-format--PBvdY ud-text-md rt-scaffolding" id="question-prompt"><p>A digital event-ticketing platform hosts its core transaction-processing service on AWS. The service runs on Amazon EC2 instances and stores finalized transactions in an Amazon Aurora PostgreSQL database. During periods of high user activity - such as flash ticket sales or holiday promotions - the application begins timing out, causing failed or delayed purchases. A solutions architect has been asked to redesign the backend for scalability and cost-efficiency, without reengineering the database layer.</p>

<p>Which combination of actions will meet these goals in the most cost-effective and scalable manner? (Select two)</p></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--question-result-pane-expanded-content--Og5Vc"><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-skipped--1NDPn" data-purpose="answer"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.6722 0.0355 279.77);"><use xlink:href="#icon-checkbox-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Deploy an Amazon API Gateway with throttling and usage plans to slow down incoming purchase requests during peak times and maintain application stability</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-skipped--1NDPn" data-purpose="answer"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.6722 0.0355 279.77);"><use xlink:href="#icon-checkbox-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Deploy read replicas for the Aurora database in another Region and configure EC2 instances to read and write from the nearest replica based on latency</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-correct--PLOEU" data-purpose="answer"><div><span data-purpose="answer-result-header-user-label" class="result-pane--answer-by-user-label--PSH86 ud-heading-xs" style="background: oklch(0.8101 0.0873 162.22); color: oklch(0.3072 0.0555 158.67);">Correct selection</span></div><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.2565 0.0265 278.04);"><use xlink:href="#icon-checkbox-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Implement Amazon RDS Proxy between the application and the Aurora PostgreSQL cluster. Deploy EC2 instances in an Auto Scaling group to retry transactions as needed</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-correct--PLOEU" data-purpose="answer"><div><span data-purpose="answer-result-header-user-label" class="result-pane--answer-by-user-label--PSH86 ud-heading-xs" style="background: oklch(0.8101 0.0873 162.22); color: oklch(0.3072 0.0555 158.67);">Correct selection</span></div><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.2565 0.0265 278.04);"><use xlink:href="#icon-checkbox-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Modify the application to publish purchase events to an Amazon SQS queue. Launch an Auto Scaling group of EC2 workers that poll the queue and process purchases asynchronously</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-skipped--1NDPn" data-purpose="answer"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.6722 0.0355 279.77);"><use xlink:href="#icon-checkbox-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Use an Amazon ElastiCache cluster to cache database queries. Configure the application to store purchase transactions in the cache before writing to the database</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--question-related-fields--c3m--"><div class="overall-explanation-pane--overall-explanation--G-hLQ ud-form-group"><label class="ud-heading-md ud-form-label ud-heading-sm" for="form-group--200">Overall explanation</label><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-text-md rt-scaffolding" id="overall-explanation"><p>Correct options:</p>

<p><strong>Implement Amazon RDS Proxy between the application and the Aurora PostgreSQL cluster. Deploy EC2 instances in an Auto Scaling group to retry transactions as needed</strong></p>

<p>Amazon RDS Proxy helps manage connection pooling and throttling, which are common causes of Aurora timeouts during high-load scenarios. It maintains a pool of database connections and reuses them across clients, reducing the overhead of frequent connection creation. Pairing this with an Auto Scaling group of EC2 instances ensures that application compute can scale dynamically based on demand. This combination improves application resiliency, reduces Aurora connection stress, and addresses peak usage efficiently and cost-effectively.</p>

<p><strong>Modify the application to publish purchase events to an Amazon SQS queue. Launch an Auto Scaling group of EC2 workers that poll the queue and process purchases asynchronously</strong></p>

<p>Introducing Amazon SQS decouples the web tier from the processing logic, allowing the system to buffer bursts in transaction load without overwhelming the database. EC2 workers in an Auto Scaling group can be dynamically scaled to consume and process queue messages based on throughput needs. This pattern ensures durability, resiliency, and elastic scalability, especially during peak usage. It's also cost-effective because compute usage grows and shrinks with actual demand.</p>

<p>Incorrect Options:</p>

<p><strong>Use an Amazon ElastiCache cluster to cache database queries. Configure the application to store purchase transactions in the cache before writing to the database</strong> - While ElastiCache is effective for read-heavy workloads, it’s not designed for durable transactional writes. Caching transactional data—especially before it is persisted in a database—risks data loss if the cache node fails. In addition, caching will not prevent database connection saturation under write-heavy load. This approach does not solve the scalability issues related to timeouts during concurrent write operations.</p>

<p><strong>Deploy an Amazon API Gateway with throttling and usage plans to slow down incoming purchase requests during peak times and maintain application stability</strong> - While API Gateway usage plans and throttling can help protect backend services from overload, they do so by delaying or rejecting traffic, which could worsen the customer experience during peak demand. This does not address the need for backend scalability, and it doesn't improve throughput or processing capacity. Instead, it suppresses demand rather than meeting it.</p>

<p><strong>Deploy read replicas for the Aurora database in another Region and configure EC2 instances to read and write from the nearest replica based on latency</strong> - This option acts as a distractor. While read replicas improve read scalability, they are read-only and cannot handle write traffic.</p>

<p>References:</p>

<p><a href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AmazonRDS/latest/UserGuide/rds-proxy.html">https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AmazonRDS/latest/UserGuide/rds-proxy.html</a></p>

<p><a href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AWSSimpleQueueService/latest/SQSDeveloperGuide/welcome.html">https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AWSSimpleQueueService/latest/SQSDeveloperGuide/welcome.html</a></p>

<p><a href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AmazonElastiCache/latest/dg/WhatIs.html">https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AmazonElastiCache/latest/dg/WhatIs.html</a></p>
</div></div><div data-purpose="domain-pane" class="domain-pane--domain-pane--Pw9dK"><div class="domain-pane--domain-pane-header--2263m ud-heading-md">Domain</div><div class="ud-text-md">Design High-Performing Architectures</div></div></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--question-result-pane-wrapper--2bGiz"><div class="result-pane--question-result-pane--sIcOh result-pane--accordion-panel--TEJg7"><div class="result-pane--question-header-wrapper--3DCpC"><div class="result-pane--question-header--pTUOx"><span class="result-pane--question-header-collapsed-text--WVdEr"><span class="result-pane--pane-title--f-2kd ud-heading-md"><span data-purpose="question-result-header-status-icon" class="result-pane--answer-status-icon--ebl6C"><span class="result-pane--question-icon-background--AskFJ" data-purpose="question-result-header-status-icon-background" style="background: oklch(0.7905 0.0283 281.19);"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-medium" style="color: oklch(0.7905 0.0283 281.19);"><use xlink:href="#icon-close"></use></svg></span></span><span>Question 34</span><span data-purpose="question-result-header-status-label" style="color: oklch(0.6722 0.0355 279.77);">Skipped</span></span><button type="button" class="ud-btn ud-btn-large ud-btn-ghost ud-btn-text-md ud-btn-icon ud-btn-icon-large"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-medium ud-icon-color-neutral"><use xlink:href="#icon-collapse"></use></svg></button></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="result-pane--question-format--PBvdY ud-text-md rt-scaffolding" id="question-prompt"><p>The product team at a startup has figured out a market need to support both stateful and stateless client-server communications via the application programming interface (APIs) developed using its platform. You have been hired by the startup as a solutions architect to build a solution to fulfill this market need using Amazon API Gateway.</p>

<p>Which of the following would you identify as correct?</p></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--question-result-pane-expanded-content--Og5Vc"><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-correct--PLOEU" data-purpose="answer"><div><span data-purpose="answer-result-header-user-label" class="result-pane--answer-by-user-label--PSH86 ud-heading-xs" style="background: oklch(0.8101 0.0873 162.22); color: oklch(0.3072 0.0555 158.67);">Correct answer</span></div><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.2565 0.0265 278.04);"><use xlink:href="#icon-radio-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Amazon API Gateway creates RESTful APIs that enable stateless client-server communication and Amazon API Gateway also creates WebSocket APIs that adhere to the WebSocket protocol, which enables stateful, full-duplex communication between client and class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg
