communication and Amazon API Gateway also creates WebSocket APIs that adhere to the WebSocket protocol, which enables stateful, full-duplex communication between client and server</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--question-related-fields--c3m--"><div class="overall-explanation-pane--overall-explanation--G-hLQ ud-form-group"><label class="ud-heading-md ud-form-label ud-heading-sm" for="form-group--202">Overall explanation</label><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-text-md rt-scaffolding" id="overall-explanation"><p>Correct option:</p>

<p><strong>Amazon API Gateway creates RESTful APIs that enable stateless client-server communication and Amazon API Gateway also creates WebSocket APIs that adhere to the WebSocket protocol, which enables stateful, full-duplex communication between client and server</strong></p>

<p>Amazon API Gateway is a fully managed service that makes it easy for developers to create, publish, maintain, monitor, and secure APIs at any scale. APIs act as the front door for applications to access data, business logic, or functionality from your backend services. Using API Gateway, you can create RESTful APIs and WebSocket APIs that enable real-time two-way communication applications.</p>

<p>How Amazon API Gateway Works:
<img src="https://d1.awsstatic.com/serverless/New-API-GW-Diagram.c9fc9835d2a9aa00ef90d0ddc4c6402a2536de0d.png" style="display: none;"><span class="ud-component--base-components--open-full-size-image"><div class="open-full-size-image--wrapper--R4gIm" data-purpose="open-full-size-image"><img src="https://d1.awsstatic.com/serverless/New-API-GW-Diagram.c9fc9835d2a9aa00ef90d0ddc4c6402a2536de0d.png" alt="" loading="eager"><button type="button" class="ud-btn ud-btn-medium ud-btn-link ud-btn-text-sm open-full-size-image--backdrop--Zor3j"><svg aria-label="Larger image" role="img" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-large ud-icon-color-neutral"><use xlink:href="#icon-search"></use></svg></button></div></span>
via - <a href="https://aws.amazon.com/api-gateway/">https://aws.amazon.com/api-gateway/</a></p>

<p>Amazon API Gateway creates RESTful APIs that:</p>

<p>Are HTTP-based.</p>

<p>Enable stateless client-server communication.</p>

<p>Implement standard HTTP methods such as GET, POST, PUT, PATCH, and DELETE.</p>

<p>Amazon API Gateway creates WebSocket APIs that:</p>

<p>Adhere to the WebSocket protocol, which enables stateful, full-duplex communication between client and server.
Route incoming messages based on message content.</p>

<p>So Amazon API Gateway supports stateless RESTful APIs as well as stateful WebSocket APIs. Therefore this option is correct.</p>

<p>Incorrect options:</p>

<p><strong>Amazon API Gateway creates RESTful APIs that enable stateful client-server communication and Amazon API Gateway also creates WebSocket APIs that adhere to the WebSocket protocol, which enables stateful, full-duplex communication between client and server</strong></p>

<p><strong>Amazon API Gateway creates RESTful APIs that enable stateless client-server communication and Amazon API Gateway also creates WebSocket APIs that adhere to the WebSocket protocol, which enables stateless, full-duplex communication between client and server</strong></p>

<p><strong>Amazon API Gateway creates RESTful APIs that enable stateful client-server communication and Amazon API Gateway also creates WebSocket APIs that adhere to the WebSocket protocol, which enables stateless, full-duplex communication between client and server</strong></p>

<p>These three options contradict the earlier details provided in the explanation. To summarize, Amazon API Gateway supports stateless RESTful APIs and stateful WebSocket APIs. Hence these options are incorrect.</p>

<p>Reference:</p>

<p><a href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/apigateway/latest/developerguide/welcome.html">https://docs.aws.amazon.com/apigateway/latest/developerguide/welcome.html</a></p>
</div></div><div data-purpose="domain-pane" class="domain-pane--domain-pane--Pw9dK"><div class="domain-pane--domain-pane-header--2263m ud-heading-md">Domain</div><div class="ud-text-md">Design High-Performing Architectures</div></div></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--question-result-pane-wrapper--2bGiz"><div class="result-pane--question-result-pane--sIcOh result-pane--accordion-panel--TEJg7"><div class="result-pane--question-header-wrapper--3DCpC"><div class="result-pane--question-header--pTUOx"><span class="result-pane--question-header-collapsed-text--WVdEr"><span class="result-pane--pane-title--f-2kd ud-heading-md"><span data-purpose="question-result-header-status-icon" class="result-pane--answer-status-icon--ebl6C"><span class="result-pane--question-icon-background--AskFJ" data-purpose="question-result-header-status-icon-background" style="background: oklch(0.7905 0.0283 281.19);"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-medium" style="color: oklch(0.7905 0.0283 281.19);"><use xlink:href="#icon-close"></use></svg></span></span><span>Question 35</span><span data-purpose="question-result-header-status-label" style="color: oklch(0.6722 0.0355 279.77);">Skipped</span></span><button type="button" class="ud-btn ud-btn-large ud-btn-ghost ud-btn-text-md ud-btn-icon ud-btn-icon-large"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-medium ud-icon-color-neutral"><use xlink:href="#icon-collapse"></use></svg></button></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="result-pane--question-format--PBvdY ud-text-md rt-scaffolding" id="question-prompt"><p>The flagship application for a gaming company connects to an Amazon Aurora database and the entire technology stack is currently deployed in the United States. Now, the company has plans to expand to Europe and Asia for its operations. It needs the <code>games</code> table to be accessible globally but needs the <code>users</code> and <code>games_played</code> tables to be regional only.</p>

<p>How would you implement this with minimal application refactoring?</p></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--question-result-pane-expanded-content--Og5Vc"><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-skipped--1NDPn" data-purpose="answer"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" Database for the <code>games</code> table and use Amazon Aurora for the <code>users</code> and <code>games_played</code> tables</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-skipped--1NDPn" data-purpose="answer"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" tables</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-skipped--1NDPn" data-purpose="answer"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.6722 0.0355 279.77);"><use xlink:href="#icon-radio-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Use a Amazon DynamoDB global table for the <code>games</code> table and use Amazon Aurora for the <code>users</code> and <code>games_played</code> tables</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--question-related-fields--c3m--"><div class="overall-explanation-pane--overall-explanation--G-hLQ ud-form-group"><label class="ud-heading-md ud-form-label ud-heading-sm" for="form-group--204">Overall explanation</label><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-text-md rt-scaffolding" id="overall-explanation"><p>Correct option:</p>

<p><strong>Use an Amazon Aurora Global Database for the <code>games</code> table and use Amazon Aurora for the <code>users</code> and <code>games_played</code> tables</strong></p>

<p>Amazon Aurora is a MySQL and PostgreSQL-compatible relational database built for the cloud, that combines the performance and availability of traditional enterprise databases with the simplicity and cost-effectiveness of open source databases. Amazon Aurora features a distributed, fault-tolerant, self-healing storage system that auto-scales up to 128TB per database instance. Aurora is not an in-memory database.</p>

<p>Amazon Aurora Global Database is designed for globally distributed applications, allowing a single Amazon Aurora database to span multiple AWS regions. It replicates your data with no impact on database performance, enables fast local reads with low latency in each region, and provides disaster recovery from region-wide outages. Amazon Aurora Global Database is the correct choice for the given use-case.</p>

<p>For the given use-case, we, therefore, need to have two Aurora clusters, one for the global table (games table) and the other one for the local tables (users and games_played tables).</p>

<p>Incorrect options:</p>

<p><strong>Use an Amazon Aurora Global Database for the <code>games</code> table and use Amazon DynamoDB tables for the <code>users</code> and <code>games_played</code> tables</strong></p>

<p><strong>Use a Amazon DynamoDB global table for the <code>games</code> table and use Amazon Aurora for the <code>users</code> and <code>games_played</code> tables</strong></p>

<p><strong>Use a Amazon DynamoDB global table for the <code>games</code> table and use Amazon DynamoDB tables for the <code>users</code> and <code>games_played</code> tables</strong></p>

<p>Here, we want minimal application refactoring. Amazon DynamoDB and Amazon Aurora have a completely different APIs, due to Amazon Aurora being SQL and Amazon DynamoDB being NoSQL. So all three options are incorrect, as they have Amazon DynamoDB as one of the components.</p>

<p>Reference:</p>

<p><a href="https://aws.amazon.com/rds/aurora/faqs/">https://aws.amazon.com/rds/aurora/faqs/</a></p>
</div></div><div data-purpose="domain-pane" class="domain-pane--domain-pane--Pw9dK"><div class="domain-pane--domain-pane-header--2263m ud-heading-md">Domain</div><div class="ud-text-md">Design Secure Architectures</div></div></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--question-result-pane-wrapper--2bGiz"><div class="result-pane--question-result-pane--sIcOh result-pane--accordion-panel--TEJg7"><div class="result-pane--question-header-wrapper--3DCpC"><div class="result-pane--question-header--pTUOx"><span class="result-pane--question-header-collapsed-text--WVdEr"><span class="result-pane--pane-title--f-2kd ud-heading-md"><span data-purpose="question-result-header-status-icon" class="result-pane--answer-status-icon--ebl6C"><span class="result-pane--question-icon-background--AskFJ" data-purpose="question-result-header-status-icon-background" style="background: oklch(0.7905 0.0283 281.19);"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-medium" style="color: oklch(0.7905 0.0283 281.19);"><use xlink:href="#icon-close"></use></svg></span></span><span>Question 36</span><span data-purpose="question-result-header-status-label" style="color: oklch(0.6722 0.0355 279.77);">Skipped</span></span><button type="button" class="ud-btn ud-btn-large ud-btn-ghost ud-btn-text-md ud-btn-icon ud-btn-icon-large"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-medium ud-icon-color-neutral"><use xlink:href="#icon-collapse"></use></svg></button></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="result-pane--question-format--PBvdY ud-text-md rt-scaffolding" id="question-prompt"><p>The DevOps team at an e-commerce company wants to perform some maintenance work on a specific Amazon EC2 instance that is part of an Auto Scaling group using a step scaling policy. The team is facing a maintenance challenge - every time the team deploys a maintenance patch, the instance health check status shows as out of service for a few minutes. This causes the Auto Scaling group to provision another replacement instance immediately.</p>

<p>As a solutions architect, which are the MOST time/resource efficient steps that you would recommend so that the maintenance work can be completed at the earliest? (Select two)</p></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--question-result-pane-expanded-content--Og5Vc"><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-skipped--1NDPn" data-purpose="answer"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.6722 0.0355 279.77);"><use xlink:href="#icon-checkbox-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Take a snapshot of the instance, create a new Amazon Machine Image (AMI) and then launch a new instance using this AMI. Apply the maintenance patch to this new instance and then add it back to the Auto Scaling Group by using the manual scaling policy. Terminate the earlier instance that had the maintenance issue</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-correct--PLOEU" data-purpose="answer"><div><span data-purpose="answer-result-header-user-label" class="result-pane--answer-by-user-label--PSH86 ud-heading-xs" style="background: oklch(0.8101 0.0873 162.22); color: oklch(0.3072 0.0555 158.67);">Correct selection</span></div><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.2565 0.0265 278.04);"><use xlink:href="#icon-checkbox-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Put the instance into the Standby state and then update the instance by applying the maintenance patch. Once the instance is ready, you can exit the Standby state and then return the instance to service</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-skipped--1NDPn" data-purpose="answer"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.6722 0.0355 279.77);"><use xlink:href="#icon-checkbox-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Suspend the <code>ScheduledActions</code> process type for the Auto Scaling group and apply the maintenance patch to the instance. Once the instance is ready, you can you can manually set the instance's health status back to healthy and activate the <code>ScheduledActions</code> process type again</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-skipped--1NDPn" data-purpose="answer"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.6722 0.0355 279.77);"><use xlink:href="#icon-checkbox-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Delete the Auto Scaling group and apply the maintenance fix to the given instance. Create a new Auto Scaling group and add all the instances again using the manual scaling policy</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-correct--PLOEU" data-purpose="answer"><div><span data-purpose="answer-result-header-user-label" class="result-pane--answer-by-user-label--PSH86 ud-heading-xs" style="background: oklch(0.8101 0.0873 162.22); color: oklch(0.3072 0.0555 158.67);">Correct selection</span></div><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.2565 0.0265 278.04);"><use xlink:href="#icon-checkbox-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Suspend the <code>ReplaceUnhealthy</code> process type for the Auto Scaling group and apply the maintenance patch to the instance. Once the instance is ready, you can manually set the instance's health status back to healthy and activate the <code>ReplaceUnhealthy</code> process type again</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--question-related-fields--c3m--"><div class="overall-explanation-pane--overall-explanation--G-hLQ ud-form-group"><label class="ud-heading-md ud-form-label ud-heading-sm" for="form-group--206">Overall explanation</label><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-text-md rt-scaffolding" id="overall-explanation"><p>Correct options:</p>

<p><strong>Put the instance into the Standby state and then update the instance by applying the maintenance patch. Once the instance is ready, you can exit the Standby state and then return the instance to service</strong> - You can put an instance that is in the <code>InService</code> state into the <code>Standby</code> state, update some software or troubleshoot the instance, and then return the instance to service. Instances that are on standby are still part of the Auto Scaling group, but they do not actively handle application traffic.</p>

<p>How Standby State Works:
<img src="https://assets-pt.media.datacumulus.com/aws-saa-pt/assets/pt1-q32-i1.jpg" style="display: none;"><span class="ud-component--base-components--open-full-size-image"><div class="open-full-size-image--wrapper--R4gIm" data-purpose="open-full-size-image"><img src="https://assets-pt.media.datacumulus.com/aws-saa-pt/assets/pt1-q32-i1.jpg" alt="" loading="eager"><button type="button" class="ud-btn ud-btn-medium ud-btn-link ud-btn-text-sm open-full-size-image--backdrop--Zor3j"><svg aria-label="Larger image" role="img" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-large ud-icon-color-neutral"><use xlink:href="#icon-search"></use></svg></button></div></span>
via - <a href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/autoscaling/ec2/userguide/as-enter-exit-standby.html">https://docs.aws.amazon.com/autoscaling/ec2/userguide/as-enter-exit-standby.html</a></p>

<p><strong>Suspend the <code>ReplaceUnhealthy</code> process type for the Auto Scaling group and apply the maintenance patch to the instance. Once the instance is ready, you can manually set the instance's health status back to healthy and activate the <code>ReplaceUnhealthy</code> process type again</strong> - The <code>ReplaceUnhealthy</code> process terminates instances that are marked as unhealthy and then creates new instances to replace them. Amazon EC2 Auto Scaling stops replacing instances that are marked as unhealthy. Instances that fail EC2 or Elastic Load Balancing health checks are still marked as unhealthy. As soon as you resume the <code>ReplaceUnhealthly</code> process, Amazon EC2 Auto Scaling replaces instances that were marked unhealthy while this process was suspended.</p>

<p>Incorrect options:</p>

<p><strong>Take a snapshot of the instance, create a new Amazon Machine Image (AMI) and then launch a new instance using this AMI. Apply the maintenance patch to this new instance and then add it back to the Auto Scaling Group by using the manual scaling policy. Terminate the earlier instance that had the maintenance issue</strong> - Taking the snapshot of the existing instance to create a new AMI and then creating a new instance in order to apply the maintenance patch is not time/resource optimal, hence this option is ruled out.</p>

<p><strong>Delete the Auto Scaling group and apply the maintenance fix to the given instance. Create a new Auto Scaling group and add all the instances again using the manual scaling policy</strong> - It's not recommended to delete the Auto Scaling group just to apply a maintenance patch on a specific instance.</p>

<p><strong>Suspend the <code>ScheduledActions</code> process type for the Auto Scaling group and apply the maintenance patch to the instance. Once the instance is ready, you can you can manually set the instance's health status back to healthy and activate the <code>ScheduledActions</code> process type again</strong> - Amazon EC2 Auto Scaling does not execute scaling actions that are scheduled to run during the suspension period. This option is not relevant to the given use-case.</p>

<p>References:</p>

<p><a href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/autoscaling/ec2/userguide/as-enter-exit-standby.html">https://docs.aws.amazon.com/autoscaling/ec2/userguide/as-enter-exit-standby.html</a></p>

<p><a href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/autoscaling/ec2/userguide/health-checks-overview.html">https://docs.aws.amazon.com/autoscaling/ec2/userguide/health-checks-overview.html</a></p>
</div></div><div data-purpose="domain-pane" class="domain-pane--domain-pane--Pw9dK"><div class="domain-pane--domain-pane-header--2263m ud-heading-md">Domain</div><div class="ud-text-md">Design Resilient Architectures</div></div></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--question-result-pane-wrapper--2bGiz"><div class="result-pane--question-result-pane--sIcOh result-pane--accordion-panel--TEJg7"><div class="result-pane--question-header-wrapper--3DCpC"><div class="result-pane--question-header--pTUOx"><span class="result-pane--question-header-collapsed-text--WVdEr"><span class="result-pane--pane-title--f-2kd ud-heading-md"><span data-purpose="question-result-header-status-icon" class="result-pane--answer-status-icon--ebl6C"><span class="result-pane--question-icon-background--AskFJ" data-purpose="question-result-header-status-icon-background" style="background: oklch(0.7905 0.0283 281.19);"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-medium" style="color: oklch(0.7905 0.0283 281.19);"><use xlink:href="#icon-close"></use></svg></span></span><span>Question 37</span><span data-purpose="question-result-header-status-label" style="color: oklch(0.6722 0.0355 279.77);">Skipped</span></span><button type="button" class="ud-btn ud-btn-large ud-btn-ghost ud-btn-text-md ud-btn-icon ud-btn-icon-large"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-medium ud-icon-color-neutral"><use xlink:href="#icon-collapse"></use></svg></button></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="result-pane--question-format--PBvdY ud-text-md rt-scaffolding" id="question-prompt"><p>A leading social media analytics company is contemplating moving its dockerized application stack into AWS Cloud. The company is not sure about the pricing for using Amazon Elastic Container Service (Amazon ECS) with the EC2 launch type compared to the Amazon Elastic Container Service (Amazon ECS) with the Fargate launch type.</p>

<p>Which of the following is correct regarding the pricing for these two services?</p></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--question-result-pane-expanded-content--Og5Vc"><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-correct--PLOEU" data-purpose="answer"><div><span data-purpose="answer-result-header-user-label" class="result-pane--answer-by-user-label--PSH86 ud-heading-xs" style="background: oklch(0.8101 0.0873 162.22); color: oklch(0.3072 0.0555 158.67);">Correct answer</span></div><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.2565 0.0265 278.04);"><use xlink:href="#icon-radio-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Amazon ECS with EC2 launch type is charged based on EC2 instances and EBS volumes used. Amazon ECS with Fargate launch type is charged based on vCPU and memory resources that the containerized application requests</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-skipped--1NDPn" data-purpose="answer"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.6722 0.0355 279.77);"><use xlink:href="#icon-radio-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Both Amazon ECS with EC2 launch type and Amazon ECS with Fargate launch type are charged based on Amazon EC2 instances and Amazon EBS Elastic Volumes used</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-skipped--1NDPn" data-purpose="answer"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.6722 0.0355 279.77);"><use xlink:href="#icon-radio-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Both Amazon ECS with EC2 launch type and Amazon ECS with Fargate launch type are charged based on vCPU and memory resources that the containerized application requests</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-skipped--1NDPn" data-purpose="answer"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.6722 0.0355 279.77);"><use xlink:href="#icon-radio-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Both Amazon ECS with EC2 launch type and Amazon ECS with Fargate launch type are just charged based on Elastic Container Service used per hour</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--question-related-fields--c3m--"><div class="overall-explanation-pane--overall-explanation--G-hLQ ud-form-group"><label class="ud-heading-md ud-form-label ud-heading-sm" for="form-group--208">Overall explanation</label><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-text-md rt-scaffolding" id="overall-explanation"><p>Correct option:</p>

<p><strong>Amazon ECS with EC2 launch type is charged based on EC2 instances and EBS volumes used. Amazon ECS with Fargate launch type is charged based on vCPU and memory resources that the containerized application requests</strong></p>

<p>Amazon Elastic Container Service (Amazon ECS) is a fully managed container orchestration service. ECS allows you to easily run, scale, and secure Docker container applications on AWS.</p>

<p>Amazon ECS Overview:
<img src="https://d1.awsstatic.com/diagrams/product-page-diagrams/product-page-diagram_ECS_1.86ebd8c223ec8b55aa1903c423fbe4e672f3daf7.png" style="display: none;"><span class="ud-component--base-components--open-full-size-image"><div class="open-full-size-image--wrapper--R4gIm" data-purpose="open-full-size-image"><img src="https://d1.awsstatic.com/diagrams/product-page-diagrams/product-page-diagram_ECS_1.86ebd8c223ec8b55aa1903c423fbe4e672f3daf7.png" alt="" loading="eager"><button type="button" class="ud-btn ud-btn-medium ud-btn-link ud-btn-text-sm open-full-size-image--backdrop--Zor3j"><svg aria-label="Larger image" role="img" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-large ud-icon-color-neutral"><use xlink:href="#icon-search"></use></svg></button></div></span>
via - <a href="https://aws.amazon.com/ecs/">https://aws.amazon.com/ecs/</a></p>

<p>With the Fargate launch type, you pay for the amount of vCPU and memory resources that your containerized application requests. vCPU and memory resources are calculated from the time your container images are pulled until the Amazon ECS Task terminates, rounded up to the nearest second.
With the EC2 launch type, there is no additional charge for the EC2 launch type. You pay for AWS resources (e.g. EC2 instances or EBS volumes) you create to store and run your application.</p>

<p>Incorrect options:</p>

<p><strong>Both Amazon ECS with EC2 launch type and Amazon ECS with Fargate launch type are charged based on vCPU and memory resources that the containerized application requests</strong></p>

<p><strong>Both Amazon ECS with EC2 launch type and Amazon ECS with Fargate launch type are charged based on Amazon EC2 instances and Amazon EBS Elastic Volumes used</strong></p>

<p>As mentioned above - with the Fargate launch type, you pay for the amount of vCPU and memory resources. With EC2 launch type, you pay for AWS resources (e.g. EC2 instances or EBS volumes). Hence both these options are incorrect.</p>

<p><strong>Both Amazon ECS with EC2 launch type and Amazon ECS with Fargate launch type are just charged based on Elastic Container Service used per hour</strong></p>

<p>This is a made-up option and has been added as a distractor.</p>

<p>References:</p>

<p><a href="https://aws.amazon.com/ecs/pricing/">https://aws.amazon.com/ecs/pricing/</a></p>
</div></div><div data-purpose="domain-pane" class="domain-pane--domain-pane--Pw9dK"><div class="domain-pane--domain-pane-header--2263m ud-heading-md">Domain</div><div class="ud-text-md">Design Cost-Optimized Architectures</div></div></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--question-result-pane-wrapper--2bGiz"><div class="result-pane--question-result-pane--sIcOh result-pane--accordion-panel--TEJg7"><div class="result-pane--question-header-wrapper--3DCpC"><div class="result-pane--question-header--pTUOx"><span class="result-pane--question-header-collapsed-text--WVdEr"><span class="result-pane--pane-title--f-2kd ud-heading-md"><span data-purpose="question-result-header-status-icon" class="result-pane--answer-status-icon--ebl6C"><span class="result-pane--question-icon-background--AskFJ" data-purpose="question-result-header-status-icon-background" style="background: oklch(0.7905 0.0283 281.19);"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-medium" style="color: oklch(0.7905 0.0283 281.19);"><use xlink:href="#icon-close"></use></svg></span></span><span>Question 38</span><span data-purpose="question-result-header-status-label" style="color: oklch(0.6722 0.0355 279.77);">Skipped</span></span><button type="button" class="ud-btn ud-btn-large ud-btn-ghost ud-btn-text-md ud-btn-icon ud-btn-icon-large"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-medium ud-icon-color-neutral"><use xlink:href="#icon-collapse"></use></svg></button></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="result-pane--question-format--PBvdY ud-text-md rt-scaffolding" id="question-prompt"><p>A biotech research company needs to perform data analytics on real-time lab results provided by a partner organization. The partner stores these lab results in an Amazon RDS for MySQL instance within the partner’s own AWS account. The research company has a private VPC that does not have internet access, Direct Connect, or a VPN connection. However, the company must establish secure and private connectivity to the RDS database in the partner’s VPC. The solution must allow the research company to connect from its VPC while minimizing complexity and complying with data security requirements.</p>

<p>Which solution will meet these requirements?</p></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--question-result-pane-expanded-content--Og5Vc"><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-skipped--1NDPn" data-purpose="answer"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.6722 0.0355 279.77);"><use xlink:href="#icon-radio-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Instruct the partner to enable public access on the Amazon RDS instance and add a security group rule to allow inbound access from the company’s IP range. The company accesses the database over the public internet through a NAT Gateway configured in a private subnet</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-skipped--1NDPn" data-purpose="answer"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.6722 0.0355 279.77);"><use xlink:href="#icon-radio-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Set up VPC peering between the company’s VPC and the partner’s VPC. Use AWS Transit Gateway in the partner's account to route traffic from the company’s VPC to the database. Modify the RDS subnet route tables to allow access from the company’s CIDR block</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-correct--PLOEU" data-purpose="answer"><div><span data-purpose="answer-result-header-user-label" class="result-pane--answer-by-user-label--PSH86 ud-heading-xs" style="background: oklch(0.8101 0.0873 162.22); color: oklch(0.3072 0.0555 158.67);">Correct answer</span></div><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.2565 0.0265 278.04);"><use xlink:href="#icon-radio-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Instruct the partner to create a Network Load Balancer (NLB) in front of the Amazon RDS for MySQL instance. Use AWS PrivateLink to expose the NLB as an interface VPC endpoint in the research company’s VPC</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-skipped--1NDPn" data-purpose="answer"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.6722 0.0355 279.77);"><use xlink:href="#icon-radio-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Configure a client VPN endpoint in the company’s account. Have researchers connect to the VPN from their local machines. Establish a Direct Connect gateway to the partner’s VPC and route RDS traffic via this connection</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--question-related-fields--c3m--"><div class="overall-explanation-pane--overall-explanation--G-hLQ ud-form-group"><label class="ud-heading-md ud-form-label ud-heading-sm" for="form-group--210">Overall explanation</label><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-text-md rt-scaffolding" id="overall-explanation"><p>Correct option:</p>

<p><strong>Instruct the partner to create a Network Load Balancer (NLB) in front of the Amazon RDS for MySQL instance. Use AWS PrivateLink to expose the NLB as an interface VPC endpoint in the research company’s VPC</strong></p>

<p>This is the correct and most secure solution. Since the RDS instance cannot be directly exposed via PrivateLink, the partner can create a Network Load Balancer (NLB) in front of a proxy or custom endpoint that connects to RDS (e.g., using RDS Proxy or an EC2-based MySQL proxy). The partner then creates a PrivateLink service (interface endpoint service) that the research company can connect to privately via an interface VPC endpoint in its own VPC. This architecture keeps traffic within the AWS network without requiring an internet gateway, VPN, or Direct Connect.</p>

<p><img src="https://assets-pt.media.datacumulus.com/aws-saa-pt/assets/pt1-q39-i2.jpg" style="display: none;"><span class="ud-component--base-components--open-full-size-image"><div class="open-full-size-image--wrapper--R4gIm" data-purpose="open-full-size-image"><img src="https://assets-pt.media.datacumulus.com/aws-saa-pt/assets/pt1-q39-i2.jpg" alt="" loading="eager"><button type="button" class="ud-btn ud-btn-medium ud-btn-link ud-btn-text-sm open-full-size-image--backdrop--Zor3j"><svg aria-label="Larger image" role="img" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-large ud-icon-color-neutral"><use xlink:href="#icon-search"></use></svg></button></div></span>
via - <a href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/vpc/latest/privatelink/what-is-privatelink.html">https://docs.aws.amazon.com/vpc/latest/privatelink/what-is-privatelink.html</a></p>

<p>Share your services through AWS PrivateLink:
<img src="https://assets-pt.media.datacumulus.com/aws-saa-pt/assets/pt1-q39-i3.jpg" style="display: none;"><span class="ud-component--base-components--open-full-size-image"><div class="open-full-size-image--wrapper--R4gIm" data-purpose="open-full-size-image"><img src="https://assets-pt.media.datacumulus.com/aws-saa-pt/assets/pt1-q39-i3.jpg" alt="" loading="eager"><button type="button" class="ud-btn ud-btn-medium ud-btn-link ud-btn-text-sm open-full-size-image--backdrop--Zor3j"><svg aria-label="Larger image" role="img" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-large ud-icon-color-neutral"><use xlink:href="#icon-search"></use></svg></button></div></span>
via - <a href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/vpc/latest/privatelink/privatelink-share-your-services.html">https://docs.aws.amazon.com/vpc/latest/privatelink/privatelink-share-your-services.html</a></p>

<p>Incorrect options:</p>

<p><strong>Instruct the partner to enable public access on the Amazon RDS instance and add a security group rule to allow inbound access from the company’s IP range. The company accesses the database over the public internet through a NAT Gateway configured in a private subnet</strong> - This option violates the requirement for no internet access in the company's VPC. Publicly exposing RDS by enabling public access and accessing it via NAT over the internet also raises serious security and compliance concerns. Furthermore, a NAT Gateway cannot exist in a subnet that has no internet gateway, making this solution infeasible in the given environment.</p>

<p><strong>Set up VPC peering between the company’s VPC and the partner’s VPC. Use AWS Transit Gateway in the partner's account to route traffic from the company’s VPC to the database. Modify the RDS subnet route tables to allow access from the company’s CIDR block</strong> - VPC peering allows direct private communication, but you cannot use Transit Gateway and VPC peering together for a single pair of VPCs—this is an architectural contradiction. You either use Transit Gateway to route traffic between VPCs or use VPC peering—not both. Additionally, RDS traffic routing through Transit Gateway requires more complex configuration and is unnecessary in this scenario.</p>

<p><strong>Configure a client VPN endpoint in the company’s account. Have researchers connect to the VPN from their local machines. Establish a Direct Connect gateway to the partner’s VPC and route RDS traffic via this connection</strong> - This option introduces multiple incorrect assumptions. First, Direct Connect is not available, as per the question’s conditions. Second, Client VPN is for user-based access, not VPC-to-VPC communication. This solution involves unnecessary complexity, adds VPN management, and fails to satisfy the requirement of connecting from the VPC itself to the RDS instance.</p>

</div></div><div data-purpose="domain-pane" class="domain-pane--domain-pane--Pw9dK"><div class="domain-pane--domain-pane-header--2263m ud-heading-md">Domain</div><div class="ud-text-md">Design Secure Architectures</div></div></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--question-result-pane-wrapper--2bGiz"><div class="result-pane--question-result-pane--sIcOh result-pane--accordion-panel--TEJg7"><div class="result-pane--question-header-wrapper--3DCpC"><div class="result-pane--question-header--pTUOx"><span class="result-pane--question-header-collapsed-text--WVdEr"><span class="result-pane--pane-title--f-2kd ud-heading-md"><span data-purpose="question-result-header-status-icon" class="result-pane--answer-status-icon--ebl6C"><span class="result-pane--question-icon-background--AskFJ" data-purpose="question-result-header-status-icon-background" style="background: oklch(0.7905 0.0283 281.19);"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-medium" style="color: oklch(0.7905 0.0283 281.19);"><use xlink:href="#icon-close"></use></svg></span></span><span>Question 39</span><span data-purpose="question-result-header-status-label" style="color: oklch(0.6722 0.0355 279.77);">Skipped</span></span><button type="button" class="ud-btn ud-btn-large ud-btn-ghost ud-btn-text-md ud-btn-icon ud-btn-icon-large"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-medium ud-icon-color-neutral"><use xlink:href="#icon-collapse"></use></svg></button></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="result-pane--question-format--PBvdY ud-text-md rt-scaffolding" id="question-prompt"><p>A new DevOps engineer has just joined a development team and wants to understand the replication capabilities for Amazon RDS Multi-AZ deployment as well as Amazon RDS Read-replicas.</p>

<p>Which of the following correctly summarizes these capabilities for the given database?</p></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--question-result-pane-expanded-content--Og5Vc"><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-skipped--1NDPn" data-purpose="answer"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.6722 0.0355 279.77);"><use xlink:href="#icon-radio-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Multi-AZ follows asynchronous replication and spans at least two Availability Zones (AZs) within a single region. Read replicas follow asynchronous replication and can be within an Availability Zone (AZ), Cross-AZ, or Cross-Region</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-skipped--1NDPn" data-purpose="answer"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.6722 0.0355 279.77);"><use xlink:href="#icon-radio-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Multi-AZ follows asynchronous replication and spans at least two Availability Zones (AZs) within a single region. Read replicas follow synchronous replication and can be within an Availability Zone (AZ), Cross-AZ, or Cross-Region</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-skipped--1NDPn" data-purpose="answer"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.6722 0.0355 279.77);"><use xlink:href="#icon-radio-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Multi-AZ follows asynchronous replication and spans one Availability Zone (AZ) within a single region. Read replicas follow synchronous replication and can be within an Availability Zone (AZ), Cross-AZ, or Cross-Region</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-correct--PLOEU" data-purpose="answer"><div><span data-purpose="answer-result-header-user-label" class="result-pane--answer-by-user-label--PSH86 ud-heading-xs" style="background: oklch(0.8101 0.0873 162.22); color: oklch(0.3072 0.0555 158.67);">Correct answer</span></div><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.2565 0.0265 278.04);"><use xlink:href="#icon-radio-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Multi-AZ follows synchronous replication and spans at least two Availability Zones (AZs) within a single region. Read replicas follow asynchronous replication and can be within an Availability Zone (AZ), Cross-AZ, or Cross-Region</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--question-related-fields--c3m--"><div class="overall-explanation-pane--overall-explanation--G-hLQ ud-form-group"><label class="ud-heading-md ud-form-label ud-heading-sm" for="form-group--212">Overall explanation</label><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-text-md rt-scaffolding" id="overall-explanation"><p>Correct option:</p>

<p><strong>Multi-AZ follows synchronous replication and spans at least two Availability Zones (AZs) within a single region. Read replicas follow asynchronous replication and can be within an Availability Zone (AZ), Cross-AZ, or Cross-Region</strong></p>

<p>Amazon RDS Multi-AZ deployments provide enhanced availability and durability for RDS database (DB) instances, making them a natural fit for production database workloads. When you provision a Multi-AZ DB Instance, Amazon RDS automatically creates a primary DB Instance and synchronously replicates the data to a standby instance in a different Availability Zone (AZ). Multi-AZ spans at least two Availability Zones (AZs) within a single region.</p>

<p>Amazon RDS Read Replicas provide enhanced performance and durability for RDS database (DB) instances. They make it easy to elastically scale out beyond the capacity constraints of a single DB instance for read-heavy database workloads. For the MySQL, MariaDB, PostgreSQL, Oracle, and SQL Server database engines, Amazon RDS creates a second DB instance using a snapshot of the source DB instance. It then uses the engines' native asynchronous replication to update the read replica whenever there is a change to the source DB instance.</p>

<p>Amazon RDS replicates all databases in the source DB instance. Read replicas can be within an Availability Zone (AZ), Cross-AZ, or Cross-Region.</p>

<p>Exam Alert:</p>

<p>Please review this comparison vis-a-vis Multi-AZ vs Read Replica for Amazon RDS:
<img src="https://assets-pt.media.datacumulus.com/aws-saa-pt/assets/pt1-q52-i1.jpg" style="display: none;"><span class="ud-component--base-components--open-full-size-image"><div class="open-full-size-image--wrapper--R4gIm" data-purpose="open-full-size-image"><img src="https://assets-pt.media.datacumulus.com/aws-saa-pt/assets/pt1-q52-i1.jpg" alt="" loading="eager"><button type="button" class="ud-btn ud-btn-medium ud-btn-link ud-btn-text-sm open-full-size-image--backdrop--Zor3j"><svg aria-label="Larger image" role="img" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-large ud-icon-color-neutral"><use xlink:href="#icon-search"></use></svg></button></div></span>
via - <a href="https://aws.amazon.com/rds/features/multi-az/">https://aws.amazon.com/rds/features/multi-az/</a></p>

<p>Incorrect Options:</p>

<p><strong>Multi-AZ follows asynchronous replication and spans one Availability Zone (AZ) within a single region. Read replicas follow synchronous replication and can be within an Availability Zone (AZ), Cross-AZ, or Cross-Region</strong></p>

<p><strong>Multi-AZ follows asynchronous replication and spans at least two Availability Zones (AZs) within a single region. Read replicas follow synchronous replication and can be within an Availability Zone (AZ), Cross-AZ, or Cross-Region</strong></p>

<p><strong>Multi-AZ follows asynchronous replication and spans at least two Availability Zones (AZs) within a single region. Read replicas follow asynchronous replication and can be within an Availability Zone (AZ), Cross-AZ, or Cross-Region</strong></p>

<p>These three options contradict the earlier details provided in the explanation. To summarize, Multi-AZ deployment follows synchronous replication for Amazon RDS. Hence these options are incorrect.</p>

Each morning, they need to transform and load the data into a data warehouse to support fast analytical queries. The company also wants to enable data analysts to build and train machine learning (ML) models using familiar SQL syntax without writing custom Python code. The architecture must support massively parallel processing (MPP) for fast data aggregation and scoring, and must use serverless AWS services wherever possible to reduce infrastructure management and operational overhead.</p>

<p>Which solution best meets these requirements?</p></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--question-result-pane-expanded-content--Og5Vc"><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-skipped--1NDPn" data-purpose="answer"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.6722 0.0355 279.77);"><use xlink:href="#icon-radio-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Run a daily AWS Glue job to process and transform the raw files in S3 and register the outputs as Amazon Athena tables in AWS Glue Data Catalog. Allow analysts to build ML models using Amazon Athena ML, with SQL-based predictions on top of S3 data without moving it to a warehouse</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-skipped--1NDPn" data-purpose="answer"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.6722 0.0355 279.77);"><use xlink:href="#icon-radio-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Use an AWS Glue job to transform and load data into Amazon RDS for PostgreSQL. Allow analysts to run machine learning models using Amazon Aurora ML integrated with PostgreSQL, leveraging Amazon SageMaker endpoints behind the scenes</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-skipped--1NDPn" data-purpose="answer"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.6722 0.0355 279.77);"><use xlink:href="#icon-radio-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Provision and run a daily Amazon EMR cluster with Apache Spark to process and transform the S3 data. Load the results into Amazon Redshift (provisioned). Enable ML model development by integrating Redshift with Amazon SageMaker notebooks for advanced modeling tasks</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-correct--PLOEU" data-purpose="answer"><div><span data-purpose="answer-result-header-user-label" class="result-pane--answer-by-user-label--PSH86 ud-heading-xs" style="background: oklch(0.8101 0.0873 162.22); color: oklch(0.3072 0.0555 158.67);">Correct answer</span></div><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.2565 0.0265 278.04);"><use xlink:href="#icon-radio-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Use a daily AWS Glue job to transform and clean the data stored in Amazon S3. Load the transformed dataset into Amazon Redshift Serverless, which offers MPP capabilities in a serverless model. Enable analysts to use Amazon Redshift ML to build and train ML models</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--question-related-fields--c3m--"><div class="overall-explanation-pane--overall-explanation--G-hLQ ud-form-group"><label class="ud-heading-md ud-form-label ud-heading-sm" for="form-group--214">Overall explanation</label><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-text-md rt-scaffolding" id="overall-explanation"><p>Correct option:</p>

<p><strong>Use a daily AWS Glue job to transform and clean the data stored in Amazon S3. Load the transformed dataset into Amazon Redshift Serverless, which offers MPP capabilities in a serverless model. Enable analysts to use Amazon Redshift ML to build and train ML models</strong></p>

<p>This solution is fully serverless and optimized for high-performance analytics and ML. AWS Glue provides serverless ETL, and Amazon Redshift Serverless offers a MPP data warehouse that scales compute independently. Amazon Redshift ML lets analysts create, train, and deploy ML models using SQL by integrating with Amazon SageMaker under the hood — abstracting away the complexity of building models. This architecture meets all core requirements: serverless, SQL-based ML, and scalable MPP analytics.</p>

<p><img src="https://assets-pt.media.datacumulus.com/aws-saa-pt/assets/pt1-q26-i1.jpg" style="display: none;"><span class="ud-component--base-components--open-full-size-image"><div class="open-full-size-image--wrapper--R4gIm" data-purpose="open-full-size-image"><img src="https://assets-pt.media.datacumulus.com/aws-saa-pt/assets/pt1-q26-i1.jpg" alt="" loading="eager"><button type="button" class="ud-btn ud-btn-medium ud-btn-link ud-btn-text-sm open-full-size-image--backdrop--Zor3j"><svg aria-label="Larger image" role="img" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-large ud-icon-color-neutral"><use xlink:href="#icon-search"></use></svg></button></div></span>
via - <a href="https://aws.amazon.com/blogs/big-data/create-train-and-deploy-machine-learning-models-in-amazon-redshift-using-sql-with-amazon-redshift-ml/">https://aws.amazon.com/blogs/big-data/create-train-and-deploy-machine-learning-models-in-amazon-redshift-using-sql-with-amazon-redshift-ml/</a></p>

<p>Incorrect options:</p>

<p><strong>Provision and run a daily Amazon EMR cluster with Apache Spark to process and transform the S3 data. Load the results into Amazon Redshift (provisioned). Enable ML model development by integrating Redshift with Amazon SageMaker notebooks for advanced modeling tasks</strong> - While EMR is suitable for large-scale transformation using Spark and Redshift supports MPP, this solution requires managing both EMR clusters and Redshift clusters. Additionally, ML modeling via SageMaker notebooks requires Python coding skills and breaks the requirement for SQL-based ML. This option introduces higher operational overhead and deviates from the serverless and SQL-only requirements.</p>

<p><strong>Run a daily AWS Glue job to process and transform the raw files in S3 and register the outputs as Amazon Athena tables in AWS Glue Data Catalog. Allow analysts to build ML models using Amazon Athena ML, with SQL-based predictions on top of S3 data without moving it to a warehouse</strong> - Although AWS Glue offers serverless ETL and RDS for PostgreSQL is widely used, RDS is not a MPP data warehouse, and performance may not scale well for large, concurrent analytical queries. While Aurora ML allows calling SageMaker models from SQL, it’s designed for transactional workloads, not large-scale ML workflows. This approach doesn't align with the analytics and MPP scale required by the company.</p>

<p><strong>Use an AWS Glue job to transform and load data into Amazon RDS for PostgreSQL. Allow analysts to run machine learning models using Amazon Aurora ML integrated with PostgreSQL, leveraging Amazon SageMaker endpoints behind the scenes</strong> - Amazon Athena is serverless and can run SQL queries on S3-based data using the Glue Data Catalog, and Athena ML allows applying SageMaker models to query outputs. However, Athena does not support MPP-level performance for large-scale data warehousing workloads and is primarily designed for ad hoc querying. Additionally, Athena ML is limited to inference only, not for training ML models via SQL.</p>
